Editor‚Äòs documentation
.

Editor‚Äòs documentation

This documentation explains the backend work needed to create ParsedClassics collections.

To understand adequately Editor‚Äòs documentation you should first study the Reader‚Äòs documentation.

Editorial roles

There are two editorial roles: senior editor and resource editor. Senior editor must know basics of HTML and Javascript coding.

Senior editor

Senior editor performs the following tasks:

- defines edition;
- defines collection and its resources;
- sends the files to work with to resource editors;
- explains tools to be used and formatting to resource editors;
- checks formatting of the files created by resource editors;
- uploads image files to the server;
- maintains Git repository;
- deploys code to the server;

Resource editor

Resource editor performs the following task:

- creates resource files.

Editor‚Äòs main tools

All editing work is being done on the localhost. The main tools are coding editor to create and edit files and web browser to view the result.

In order to start to work on ParsedClassics project, the editor should place the copy of ParsedClassics app into some directory on localhost, open /app.html file in web browser and fire the coding editor program. The editing work consists in making edits in the code editor, saving and previewing results in the web browser.

Coding editor software

Any HTML/CSS/Javascript coding editor software is suitable for ParsedClassics projects. We recommend VS Code (Win/Mac, free).

Greek polytonic keyboard

To type Greek characters Greek polytonic keyboard software should be used. It is recommended to use virtual Greek polytonic keyboard, because it implements encoding conventions required for resources of ParsedClassics collections.

Web browser

Any major modern webbrowser ‚Äì Chrome, Firefox, Opera, Safari ‚Äì is suitable for previewing ParsedClassics projects on localhost. Among them Firefox has certain advantage: it preserves form values while reloading the page. But in Firefox default security settings may prevent the webfonts to be rendered in localhost environment. To see correct font in Firefox in localhost environment go to about:config and change the value of security.fileuri.strict_origin_policy to "false":

Git client and code deployment tool

For maintaining and deploying the code senior will need Git client and deployment tool.

As simple and convenient Git client can be recommended Github desktop app (Win/Mac, free).

As simple and convenient code deployment tool the online service launchdeck.io can be recommended.

Defining edition

To define a new edition senior editor should add JSON object into the file /data/_catalogues/_sets.js . The order of JSON objects in this file is important because Catalogue page displays the list of editions in the same order.

For example, to define the edition "·º© ŒöŒ±ŒπŒΩ·Ω¥ ŒîŒπŒ±Œ∏ŒÆŒ∫Œ∑. ŒÝœÅ·Ω±ŒæŒµŒπœÇ, ·ºòœÄŒπœÉœÑŒøŒªŒ±ŒØ, ·ºàœÄŒøŒ∫·Ω±ŒªœÖœàŒπœÇ / The New Testament. Acts, Epistles, Revelation" such JSON object has been added:

  nt_apostolics: {
    title_orig: '·º© ŒöŒ±ŒπŒΩ·Ω¥ ŒîŒπŒ±Œ∏ŒÆŒ∫Œ∑. ŒÝœÅ·Ω±ŒæŒµŒπœÇ, ·ºòœÄŒπœÉœÑŒøŒªŒ±ŒØ, ·ºàœÄŒøŒ∫·Ω±ŒªœÖœàŒπœÇ',
    title_orig_short: 'Œö.Œî. ŒÝœÅ·Ω±ŒæŒµŒπœÇ, ·ºòœÄŒπœÉœÑŒøŒªŒ±ŒØ, ·ºàœÄŒøŒ∫·Ω±ŒªœÖœàŒπœÇ',
    title_eng: 'The New Testament. Acts, Epistles, Revelation',	
    collections: [],	
  },

The value of the key "title_orig" should be a string in original language. It should include author or scripture name and the title. Abbreviation or/and shortened title can be used in order to avoid very long value. This value will be used in Catalogue page.

The value of the key "title_orig_short" should be a string in original language. This value usually is shorter than the value of the key "title_orig". Abbreviation or/and shortened title can be used in order to avoid very long value. This value will be used inside Collections selectbox at Library app page.

The value of the key "title_eng" should be a string in English. It should include author or scripture name and the title. Abbreviation or/and shortened title can be used in order to avoid very long value. This value will be used in Catalogue page.

The value of the key "collections" should be array of strings which are shortnames of collections. For now let's leave this array empty; we will add member to this array after defining certain collection.

After editing /data/_catalogues/_sets.js file refresh Catalogue page. A new value should appear in editions list.

Defining collection and its resources

Defining collection and its resources consists of the following tasks:
(1) listing collection;
(2) registering collection as part of edition;
(3) creating empty collection catalogue;
(4) listing collection resources;
(5) listing scanned books.

Listing collection

To list a new collection senior editor should add JSON object into the file /data/_catalogues/_collections.js as the value of certain key of ParsedClassicsCollDefs object.

For example, to list the collection Epistle to Titus such JSON object has been added as the value of the key "nt_titus":

const ParsedClassicsCollDefs = {
  
  // some lines have been omitted

  nt_titus: {
    author_orig: '·º© ŒöŒ±ŒπŒΩ·Ω¥ ŒîŒπŒ±Œ∏ŒÆŒ∫Œ∑',   
    author_eng: 'The New Testament',
    collection_selectboxname: 'Œö.Œî. ŒÝœÅ·Ω∏œÇ Œ§ŒØœÑŒøŒΩ',
    collections_page_title_orig: 'ŒÝŒ±·ΩªŒªŒøœÖ œÑŒø·ø¶ ·ºÄœÄŒøœÉœÑ·ΩπŒªŒøœÖ ·º° œÄœÅ·Ω∏œÇ Œ§ŒØœÑŒøŒΩ ·ºêœÄŒπœÉœÑŒøŒªŒÆ',
    collections_page_title_eng: 'Apostle Paul\'s epistle to Titus', 
  },
  
  // some lines have been omitted

}

The key used to list collection let's call "collection shortname". This is important term and will be used often in this documentation.

Collection shortname should be a string containing only lowercase latin letters, numbers and underscores (no spaces!). It should include author or scripture name and the title. Abbreviation or/and shortened title can be used in order to avoid very long value.

The value of the key "collection_selectboxname" should be a string in original language. It should include author or scripture name and the title. Abbreviation or/and shortened title can be used in order to avoid very long value. It will be displayed in Collections selectbox.

The key "collections_page_title_eng" should have as its value the title of the collection in English.

The key "collections_page_title_orig" should have as its value the title of the collection in original language.

Both English and original title will be displayed in Collections page. Original title will also be displayed as title of parsed text resource.

The key "author_orig" should have as its value the name of the author or the name of the scripture in original language, i. e. in Greek or Latin. It will be displayed as author name of parsed text resource.

The key "author_eng" should have as its value English name of the author or English name of the scripture. The value is currently not used.

Since classics text usually consists of several books and each book usually will have its own collection, the values of the keys "author_orig" and "author_eng" will be repeated listing those collections. In order to avoid repetitions it is recommended to define JSON object containing all keys whose values would be repeated. That JSON object should be the value of certain key of ParsedClassicsCollProtos object which is in the same file as ParsedClassicsCollDefs object. Since the values of the keys "author_orig" and "author_eng" will be repeated for all NT books, let's name the key "nt_book":

  const ParsedClassicsCollProtos = {

    // some lines have been omitted

    nt_book: {
      author_orig: '·º© ŒöŒ±ŒπŒΩ·Ω¥ ŒîŒπŒ±Œ∏ŒÆŒ∫Œ∑',   
      author_eng: 'The New Testament',
    },

    // some lines have been omitted
  
  };

Now we can destructure the object ParsedClassicsCollProtos.nt_book anywhere we need the same values of "author_orig" and "author_eng" keys:

  const ParsedClassicsCollDefs = {
    
    // some lines have been omitted
  
    nt_titus: {
      ...ParsedClassicsCollProtos.nt_book,
      collection_selectboxname: 'Œö.Œî. ŒÝœÅ·Ω∏œÇ Œ§ŒØœÑŒøŒΩ',
      collections_page_title_orig: 'ŒÝŒ±·ΩªŒªŒøœÖ œÑŒø·ø¶ ·ºÄœÄŒøœÉœÑ·ΩπŒªŒøœÖ ·º° œÄœÅ·Ω∏œÇ Œ§ŒØœÑŒøŒΩ ·ºêœÄŒπœÉœÑŒøŒªŒÆ',
      collections_page_title_eng: 'Apostle Paul\'s epistle to Titus', 
    },
    
    // some lines have been omitted
  
  }

Registering collection

The collection we just listed among other collections should be registered as a part of edition. This should be done by entering collection shortname as member of array which is value of the key "collections" in edition's definition:

  nt_apostolics: {
    title_orig: '·º© ŒöŒ±ŒπŒΩ·Ω¥ ŒîŒπŒ±Œ∏ŒÆŒ∫Œ∑. ŒÝœÅ·Ω±ŒæŒµŒπœÇ, ·ºòœÄŒπœÉœÑŒøŒªŒ±ŒØ, ·ºàœÄŒøŒ∫·Ω±ŒªœÖœàŒπœÇ',
    title_orig_short: 'Œö.Œî. ŒÝœÅ·Ω±ŒæŒµŒπœÇ, ·ºòœÄŒπœÉœÑŒøŒªŒ±ŒØ, ·ºàœÄŒøŒ∫·Ω±ŒªœÖœàŒπœÇ',
    title_eng: 'The New Testament. Acts, Epistles, Revelation',	
    collections: [
      'nt_titus',
    ],	
  },

The order of collection shortnames is important, because list of collections will be displayed in that order.

Creating empty collection catalogue

Collection catalogue is a file inside /data/_catalogues/ directory. Collection catalogue‚Äòs filename should be the same as the collection shortname. In the example above collection shortname was "nt_titus". That means the name of the file of the collection catalogue should be "nt_titus.js".

The encoding of the collection catalogue file must be UTF-8 (no BOM).

Let‚Äòs as example to create catalogue for Epistle to Titus collection.

To create empty catalogue for this collection we need to add to the object ParsedClassicsCollDefs the key "nt_titus" and to the object "nt_titus" the object "resource_defs"; let's also indicate the order of resource types:

ParsedClassicsCollDefs.nt_titus["resource_defs"] = {
  // Parsed text
  // IMPORTANT!
  // The contents of the first resource of the type "Parsed text" serves as contents of the whole collection
  
  // Original texts

  // Concordances

  // Lexicons

  // Translations

  // Commentaries

  // Commentary references

  // Grammar references

  // Diagram sets

  // Audio
}

Listing collection resources

The catalogue just created is empty because no resource is listed in it. Library app supports following types of resources: Parsed text, Critical edition, Concordance, Lexicon, Translation, Commentary, Commentary references, Grammar references, Diagram set, Audio recording.

Parsed text

As an example let‚Äòs list parsed text resource for Epistle to Titus collection. Todo it we need to add JSON object as the value of certain key of ParsedClassicsCollDefs.nt_titus["resource_defs"] object. The key used to list resource let's call "resource shortname". This is important term and will be used often in this documentation.

In this case the key is "nt_titus_parsed_text" (contains inside collection shortname and resource type):

  ParsedClassicsCollDefs.nt_titus["resource_defs"] = {
    // Parsed text
    // IMPORTANT!
    // The contents of the first resource of the type "Parsed text" serves as contents of the whole collection

    nt_titus_parsed_text: {
      collections_page_resource_desc: "ed. by ParsedClassics (2018)",
      library_app_selectbox_title: "Byzantine textform", 
      library_app_panel_subtitle: "",
      library_app_panel_text_from: "The New Testament in the original Greek. Byzantine textform. Compiled and arranged by M. A. Robinson and W. G. Pierpont. 2005. Southborough, MA: Chilton book publishing.",
      library_app_panel_note: "",
      scanned_or_typed: "typed",
      resource_type: "parsed_text",
      scanned_source_shortname: "new_testament_in_original_greek_ed_robinson_pierpont",
      library_app_panel_title: "ŒÝŒ±·ΩªŒªŒøœÖ œÑŒø·ø¶ ·ºÄœÄŒøœÉœÑ·ΩπŒªŒøœÖ ·º° œÄœÅ·Ω∏œÇ Œ§ŒØœÑŒøŒΩ ·ºêœÄŒπœÉœÑŒøŒªŒÆ",
      contents_shortname: "nt_titus_parsed_text_contents",
    },
    
    // some lines have been omitted
  }

After you add these lines, you should see this resource listed in Resources selectbox and in Collections page.

The key "collections_page_resource_desc" should have as its value a string "ed. by" plus compilator‚Äòs name and the year in brackets.

The key "library_app_panel_title" should have as its value the title of the resource in original language.

The key "library_app_panel_subtitle" should have as its value the subtitle of the resource in original language. Here this key has empty string value because resource has no subtitle.

The key "library_app_panel_text_from" should have as its value bibliographic description of the book from which the text for parsing was taken.

The key "library_app_panel_note" should have as its value some text. Most probably it will be some acknowledgments.

The key "scanned_or_typed" should have as its value the string "typed" (it means "transcribed").

The key "scanned_source_shortname" should have as its value the name of the directory (without path) in which has been uploaded the images of the pages of the book from which the text for parsing was taken. Directory name includes title of the book, string "ed" and names of the authors.

The key "library_app_selectbox_title" should have as its value short English title of the resource.

The key "resource_type" should have the value "parsed_text".

The key "contents_shortname" should have as its value the name of the file containing resource's contents. The name of this file is usually formed by adding the string "parsed_text" at the end of collection name and next adding the string "contents" or the string indicating resource and the string "contents". So, if the collection shortname was "nt_titus", the the name of parsed text resource contents file will be "nt_titus_parsed_text_contents" or "nt_titus_parsed_text_byzantine_contents". About creating contents file and placing it in directory will be explaided below. [LINK TO BE ADDED]

Since classics text usually consists of several books and each book usually will have its own collection with its own parsed text resource, the values of the many keys will be repeated listing those resources. In order to avoid repetitions it is recommended to define JSON object containing all keys whose values would be repeated. That JSON object should be the value of certain key of ParsedClassicsResProtos object which is in the file /data/_catalogues/_res_protos.js . Since the values of many keys will be repeated for all resources of the type "Parsed text" based on Byzantyne textform, let's name the key "nt_parsed_text_byzantine":

const ParsedClassicsResProtos = {
  // Parsed texts

  nt_parsed_text_byzantine: {
    collections_page_resource_desc: "ed. by ParsedClassics (2018)",
    library_app_selectbox_title: "Byzantine textform", 
    library_app_panel_subtitle: "",
    library_app_panel_text_from: "The New Testament in the original Greek. Byzantine textform. Compiled and arranged by M. A. Robinson and W. G. Pierpont. 2005. Southborough, MA: Chilton book publishing.",
    library_app_panel_note: "",
    scanned_or_typed: "typed",
    resource_type: "parsed_text",
    scanned_source_shortname: "new_testament_in_original_greek_ed_robinson_pierpont", 
  },

  // some lines have been omitted
}

Now we can destructure the object ParsedClassicsCollProtos.nt_parsed_text_byzantine anywhere we need the same values of its keys:

  ParsedClassicsCollDefs.nt_titus["resource_defs"] = {
    // Parsed text
    // IMPORTANT!
    // The contents of the first resource of the type "Parsed text" serves as contents of the whole collection

    nt_titus_parsed_text: {
      ...ParsedClassicsResProtos.nt_parsed_text_byzantine,
      library_app_panel_title: "ŒÝŒ±·ΩªŒªŒøœÖ œÑŒø·ø¶ ·ºÄœÄŒøœÉœÑ·ΩπŒªŒøœÖ ·º° œÄœÅ·Ω∏œÇ Œ§ŒØœÑŒøŒΩ ·ºêœÄŒπœÉœÑŒøŒªŒÆ",
      contents_shortname: "nt_titus_parsed_text_contents",
    },
    
    // some lines have been omitted
  }

Original text

There can be several original text resources inside collection. In principle, resources belonging to type "Original text" can be either scanned or transcribed, but they surely will be all scanned because it is very difficult to reproduce complex formatting of the scholarly editions using very limitted means available in HTML.

As an example let‚Äòs list original text resource for Epistle to Titus collection. Todo it we need to add JSON object as the value of certain key of ParsedClassicsCollDefs.nt_titus["resource_defs"] object. In this case the key (resource shortnamw) is "nt_titus_text_ed_antoniadis" (contains inside collection shortname, resource type and editor's name):

ParsedClassicsCollDefs.nt_titus["resource_defs"] = {
  // some lines have been omitted

  // Original texts

  nt_titus_text_ed_antoniadis: {
    collections_page_resource_desc: "ed. by V. Antoniadis (1904)", 
    library_app_selectbox_title: "Edition by V. Antoniadis (1904)",
    library_app_panel_title: "Text ed. by V. Antoniadis (1904)",
    library_app_panel_subtitle: "",
    library_app_panel_text_from: "·º© ŒöŒ±ŒπŒΩ·Ω¥ ŒîŒπŒ±Œ∏ŒÆŒ∫Œ∑ ·ºêŒ≥Œ∫œÅŒØœÉŒµŒπ œÑ·øÜœÇ ŒúŒµŒ≥Œ¨ŒªŒ∑œÇ œÑŒø·ø¶ ŒßœÅŒπœÉœÑŒø·ø¶ ·ºòŒ∫Œ∫ŒªŒ∑œÉŒØŒ±œÇ. 1912. ·ºòŒΩ ŒöœâŒΩœÉœÑŒ±ŒΩœÑŒπŒΩŒøœÖœÄœåŒªŒµŒπ. ·ºòŒ∫ œÑŒø·ø¶ ŒÝŒ±œÑœÅŒπŒ±œáŒπŒ∫Œø·ø¶ Œ§œÖœÄŒøŒ≥œÅŒ±œÜŒµŒØŒøœÖ.",
    library_app_panel_note: "",
    scanned_or_typed: "scanned",
    resource_type: "original_text",
    scanned_source_shortname: "kaine_diatheke_ed_antoniadis",
    contents_shortname: "nt_titus_ed_antoniadis_contents",
  },

  // some lines have been omitted
}

After you add these lines, you should see this resource listed in Resources selectbox and in Collections page.

The key "collections_page_resource_desc" should have as its value a string "ed. by" plus editor‚Äòs name and the year in brackets.

The key "library_app_panel_title" should have as its value short title of the resource in English.

The key "library_app_panel_subtitle" should have as its value short subtitle of the resource. Here this key has empty string value because resource has no subtitle.

The key "library_app_panel_text_from" should have as its value bibliographic description of the book.

The key "library_app_panel_note" should have as its value some text. Most probably it will be some acknowledgments.

The key "scanned_or_typed" should have as its value the string "scanned".

The key "scanned_source_shortname" should have as its value the name of the directory (without path) in which has been uploaded the images of the pages of the book. Directory name includes title of the book, string "ed" and name of the author.

The key "library_app_selectbox_title" should have as its value short English title of the resource.

The key "resource_type" should have the value "original_text".

The key "contents_shortname" should have as its value the name of the file containing resource's contents. The name of this file is usually formed by adding the string "ed" at the end of collection name, then adding name of editor and next adding the string "contents". So, if the collection shortname was "nt_titus", and the editor was Antoniadis, then the name of original text resource contents file will be "nt_titus_ed_antoniadis_contents". About creating contents file and placing it in directory will be explained below. [LINK TO BE ADDED]

Since classics text usually consists of several books and each book usually will have its own collection with its own original text resource, the values of many keys will be repeated listing those resources. In order to avoid repetitions it is recommended to define JSON object containing all keys whose values would be repeated. That JSON object should be the value of certain key of ParsedClassicsResProtos object which is in the file /data/_catalogues/_res_protos.js . Since the values of many keys will be repeated for all resources of the type "Original text" based on edition by Antoniadis, let's name the key "nt_text_ed_antoniadis":

const ParsedClassicsResProtos = {
  // Original texts

  nt_text_ed_antoniadis: {
    collections_page_resource_desc: "ed. by V. Antoniadis (1904)", 
    library_app_selectbox_title: "Edition by V. Antoniadis (1904)",
    library_app_panel_title: "Text ed. by V. Antoniadis (1904)",
    library_app_panel_subtitle: "",
    library_app_panel_text_from: "·º© ŒöŒ±ŒπŒΩ·Ω¥ ŒîŒπŒ±Œ∏ŒÆŒ∫Œ∑ ·ºêŒ≥Œ∫œÅŒØœÉŒµŒπ œÑ·øÜœÇ ŒúŒµŒ≥Œ¨ŒªŒ∑œÇ œÑŒø·ø¶ ŒßœÅŒπœÉœÑŒø·ø¶ ·ºòŒ∫Œ∫ŒªŒ∑œÉŒØŒ±œÇ. 1912. ·ºòŒΩ ŒöœâŒΩœÉœÑŒ±ŒΩœÑŒπŒΩŒøœÖœÄœåŒªŒµŒπ. ·ºòŒ∫ œÑŒø·ø¶ ŒÝŒ±œÑœÅŒπŒ±œáŒπŒ∫Œø·ø¶ Œ§œÖœÄŒøŒ≥œÅŒ±œÜŒµŒØŒøœÖ.",
    library_app_panel_note: "",
    scanned_or_typed: "scanned",
    resource_type: "original_text",
    scanned_source_shortname: "kaine_diatheke_ed_antoniadis",
  },

  // some lines have been omitted
}

Now we can destructure the object ParsedClassicsCollProtos.nt_text_ed_antoniadis anywhere we need the same values of its keys:

ParsedClassicsCollDefs.nt_titus["resource_defs"] = {
  // some lines have been omitted

  // Original texts

  nt_titus_text_ed_antoniadis: {
    ...ParsedClassicsResProtos.nt_text_ed_antoniadis,
    contents_shortname: "nt_titus_ed_antoniadis_contents",
  },

  // some lines have been omitted
}

Concordance

There can be many concordances inside a collection. Resource belonging to the type "Concordance" can be either scanned or transcribed.

As examples let‚Äòs list scanned and transcribed concordance resources for Epistle to Titus collection. To do it we need to add JSON objects as the values of certain keys of ParsedClassicsCollDefs.nt_titus["resource_defs"] object. In this case the keys (resource shortnames) are "concordance_by_moulton_geden" and "nt_conc_by_parsedclassics" (contains inside resource type and editor's name):

ParsedClassicsCollDefs.nt_titus["resource_defs"] = {
  // some lines have been omitted

  // Concordances

  concordance_by_moulton_geden: {
    collections_page_resource_desc: "ed. by W. F. Moulton and A. S. Geden (1899)", 
    library_app_selectbox_title: "Concordance ed. by W. F. Moulton and A. S. Geden (1899)",
    library_app_panel_title: "A concordance to the Greek Testament ed. by W. F. Moulton and A. S. Geden (1899)",
    library_app_panel_text_from: "A concordance to the Greek Testament according to the texts of Westcott and Hort, Tischendorf and the English Revisers. Edited by W. F. Moulton and A. S. Geden. 2-nd ed. 1899. Edinburgh: T. & T. Clark.",
    library_app_panel_note: "",
    scanned_or_typed: "scanned",
    resource_type: "concordance",
    scanned_source_shortname: "concordance_to_greek_testament_by_moulton_geden",
    contents_shortname: "concordance_to_greek_testament_by_moulton_geden_contents",
  },

  nt_conc_by_parsedclassics: {
    collections_page_resource_desc: "compiled by ParsedClassics (2018)", 
    library_app_selectbox_title: "Concordance compiled by ParsedClassics (2018)",
    library_app_panel_title: "New Testament concordance",
    library_app_panel_text_from: "",
    library_app_panel_note: "Compiled by ParsedClassics (2018)",
    scanned_or_typed: "typed",
    resource_type: "concordance",
    scanned_source_shortname: "",
    contents_shortname: "nt_conc_by_parsedclassics_contents",
  },

  // some lines have been omitted

}

After you add these lines, you should see these resources listed in Resources selectbox and in Collections page.

For scanned concordance resource the key "collections_page_resource_desc" should have as its value a string "ed. by" plus compilator‚Äòs name and the year in brackets. For transcribed concordance resource the key "collections_page_resource_desc" should have as its value a string "compiled by" plus compilator‚Äòs name and the year in brackets.

The key "library_app_panel_title" should have as its value short title of the resource in English.

The key "library_app_panel_subtitle" should have as its value short subtitle of the resource. Here this key has empty string value because resources has no subtitle.

The key "library_app_panel_text_from" should have as its value bibliographic description of the book.

The key "library_app_panel_note" should have as its value some text. Most probably it will be some acknowledgments. For transcribed concordance resource the value should be a string "Compiled by" plus compilator‚Äòs name and the year in brackets.

The key "scanned_or_typed" should have as its value the string "scanned" for scanned resource and "typed" for transcribed resource.

The key "scanned_source_shortname" should have as its value the name of the directory (without path) in which has been uploaded the images of the pages of the book. Directory name includes title of the book, string "by" and names of the authors. For transcribed concordance resource the value of this key should be an empty string.

The key "library_app_selectbox_title" should have as its value short English title of the resource.

The key "resource_type" should have the value "concordance".

The key "contents_shortname" should have as its value the name of the file containing resource's contents. The name of this file is usually formed by adding the string "by" at the end of short title, then adding name of author or compiler and next adding the string "contents". About creating contents file and placing it in directory will be explained below. [LINK TO BE ADDED]

Classics text usually consists of several books and each book usually will have its own collection. If we have certain concordance resource, it will be listed in all of these collections. That means there is no need to use ParsedClassicsResProtos object in listing concordance resources.

Lexicon

There can be many lexicons inside a collection. Resource belonging to the type "Lexicon" can be either scanned or transcribed.

As examples let‚Äòs list scanned and transcribed lexicon resources for Epistle to Titus collection. To do it we need to add JSON objects as the values of certain keys of ParsedClassicsCollDefs.nt_titus["resource_defs"] object. In this case the keys (resource shortnames) are "greek_lexicon_of_nt_by_robinson" and "greek_lexicon_to_nt_by_green" (contains inside short title and author's name):

ParsedClassicsCollDefs.nt_titus["resource_defs"] = {
  // some lines have been omitted

  // Lexicons

  greek_lexicon_of_nt_by_robinson: {
    collections_page_resource_desc: "Greek-English lexicon of the NT by E. Robinson (1850)", 
    library_app_selectbox_title: "Greek-English lexicon of the NT by E. Robinson (1850)",
    library_app_panel_title: "A Greek and English lexicon of the New Testament by E. Robinson (1850)",
    library_app_panel_text_from: "A Greek and English lexicon of the New Testament. By Edward Robinson. Second edition. 1850. New York: Harper and Brothers.",
    library_app_panel_note: "",
    scanned_or_typed: "scanned",
    resource_type: "lexicon",
    scanned_source_shortname: "greek_and_english_lexicon_of_nt_by_robinson", 
    contents_shortname: "greek_and_english_lexicon_of_nt_by_robinson_contents",
  },

  greek_lexicon_to_nt_by_green: {
    collections_page_resource_desc: "Greek-English lexicon of the NT by Th. S. Green (1896)", 
    library_app_selectbox_title: "Greek-English lexicon of the NT by Th. S. Green (1896)",
    library_app_panel_title: "A Greek-English lexicon to the New Testament by Th. S. Green (1896)",
    library_app_panel_text_from: "A Greek-English lexicon to the New Testament. Revised and enlarged by Thomas Sheldon Green. 1896. Boston: H. L. Hastings.",
    library_app_panel_note: "",
    scanned_or_typed: "typed",
    resource_type: "lexicon",
    scanned_source_shortname: "greek_english_lexicon_to_nt_by_green", 
    contents_shortname: "",
  },

  // some lines have been omitted

}

After you add these lines, you should see these resources listed in Resources selectbox and in Collections page.

The key "collections_page_resource_desc" should have as its value short title plus the string "by" plus author‚Äòs name and the year in brackets.

The key "library_app_panel_title" should have as its value short title plus the string "by" plus author‚Äòs name and the year in brackets.

The key "library_app_panel_subtitle" should have as its value short subtitle of the resource. Here this key has empty string value because resources has no subtitle.

The key "library_app_panel_text_from" should have as its value bibliographic description of the book.

The key "library_app_panel_note" should have as its value some text. Most probably it will be some acknowledgments.

The key "scanned_or_typed" should have as its value the string "scanned" for scanned resource and "typed" for transcribed resource.

The key "scanned_source_shortname" should have as its value the name of the directory (without path) in which have been uploaded the images of the pages of the book. Directory name includes title of the book, string "by" and name of the author.

The key "library_app_selectbox_title" should have as its value short English title of the resource plus the string "by" plus author‚Äòs name and the year in brackets.

The key "resource_type" should have the value "lexicon".

The key "contents_shortname" for scanned lexicon resource should have as its value the name of the file containing resource's contents. The name of this file is usually formed by adding the string "by" at the end of short title, then adding name of author and next adding the string "contents". About creating contents file and placing it in directory will be explained below. [LINK TO BE ADDED] The key "contents_shortname" for transcribed lexicon resource should have as its value an empty string.

Classics text usually consists of several books and each book usually will have its own collection. If we have certain lexicon resource, it will be listed in all of these collections. That means there is no need to use ParsedClassicsResProtos object in listing lexicon resources.

Translation

There can be several translation resources inside collection. In principle, resources belonging to type "Translation" can be either scanned or transcribed, but they most surely will be all scanned because there is little sense in transcribing translation of classics text.

As an example let‚Äòs list translation resource for Epistle to Titus collection. Todo it we need to add JSON object as the value of certain key of ParsedClassicsCollDefs.nt_titus["resource_defs"] object. In this case the key is "nt_titus_tr_EN_young" (contains inside collection shortname, string "tr", code of the language and and translator's name):

ParsedClassicsCollDefs.nt_titus["resource_defs"] = {
  // some lines have been omitted

  // Translations

  nt_titus_tr_EN_young: {
    collections_page_resource_desc: "to English by R. Young (1898)", 
    library_app_selectbox_title: "Translation to English by  R. Young (1898)",
    library_app_panel_title: "English translation by R. Young (1898)",
    library_app_panel_subtitle: "",
    library_app_panel_text_from: "The Holy Bible, consisting of the Old and New Covenants, translated according to the letter and idiom of the original languages by Robert Young. Revised edition. 1898. Edinburgh: G. A. Young and Co.",
    library_app_panel_note: "",
    scanned_or_typed: "scanned",
    resource_type: "translation",
    scanned_source_shortname: "holy_bible_tr_young",
    contents_shortname: "nt_titus_tr_EN_young_contents",
  },

  // some lines have been omitted
}

After you add these lines, you should see this resource listed in Resources selectbox and in Collections page.

The key "collections_page_resource_desc" should have as its value a string "to" plus language plus "by" plus translator‚Äòs name and the year in brackets.

The key "library_app_panel_title" should have as its value the language plus "translation by" plus translator‚Äòs name and the year in brackets.

The key "library_app_panel_subtitle" should have as its value short subtitle of the resource. Here this key has empty string value because resource has no subtitle.

The key "library_app_panel_text_from" should have as its value bibliographic description of the book.

The key "library_app_panel_note" should have as its value some text. Most probably it will be some acknowledgments.

The key "scanned_or_typed" should have as its value the string "scanned".

The key "scanned_source_shortname" should have as its value the name of the directory (without path) in which has been uploaded the images of the pages of the book. Directory name includes short title of the book, string "tr" and name of the translator.

The key "library_app_selectbox_title" should have as its value string "Translation to" then language then "by" then translator's name and year in brackets.

The key "resource_type" should have the value "translation".

The key "contents_shortname" should have as its value the name of the file containing resource's contents. The name of this file is usually formed by adding the string "tr" at the end of collection name, then adding lamguage, name of translator and last adding the string "contents". So, if the collection shortname was "nt_titus", and the editor was Young who translated to English, then the name of translation resource contents file will be "nt_titus_tr_EN_young_contents". Creating contents file and placing it in directory will be explaided below. [LINK TO BE ADDED]

Since classics text usually consists of several books and each book usually will have its own collection with its own translation resource, the values of the many keys will be repeated listing those translation resources. In order to avoid repetitions it is recommended to define JSON object containing all keys whose values would be repeated. That JSON object should be the value of certain key of ParsedClassicsResProtos object which is in the file /data/_catalogues/_res_protos.js . Since the values of many keys will be repeated for all New Testament resources of the type "Translation" based on translation by Young, let's name the key "nt_tr_EN_young":

const ParsedClassicsResProtos = {
  // Translation

  // some lines have been omitted

  nt_tr_EN_young: {
    collections_page_resource_desc: "to English by R. Young (1898)", 
    library_app_selectbox_title: "Translation to English by  R. Young (1898)",
    library_app_panel_title: "English translation by R. Young (1898)",
    library_app_panel_subtitle: "",
    library_app_panel_text_from: "The Holy Bible, consisting of the Old and New Covenants, translated according to the letter and idiom of the original languages by Robert Young. Revised edition. 1898. Edinburgh: G. A. Young and Co.",
    library_app_panel_note: "",
    scanned_or_typed: "scanned",
    resource_type: "translation",
    scanned_source_shortname: "holy_bible_tr_young",
  },

  // some lines have been omitted
}

Now we can destructure the object ParsedClassicsCollProtos.nt_tr_EN_young anywhere we need the same values of its keys:

ParsedClassicsCollDefs.nt_titus["resource_defs"] = {
  // some lines have been omitted

  // Translations

  nt_titus_tr_EN_young: {
    ...ParsedClassicsResProtos.nt_tr_EN_young,
    contents_shortname: "nt_titus_tr_EN_young_contents",
  },

  // some lines have been omitted
}

Commentary

There can be several commentary resources inside collection. In principle, resources belonging to type "Commentary" can be either scanned or transcribed, but they most surely will be all scanned because there is little sense in transcribing commentary of classics text.

As an example let‚Äòs list commentary resource for Epistle to Titus collection. Todo it we need to add JSON object as the value of certain key of ParsedClassicsCollDefs.nt_titus["resource_defs"] object. In this case the key (resource shortname) is "nt_titus_commentary_by_nicoll" (contains inside collection shortname, type of resource, string "by" and author's name):

ParsedClassicsCollDefs.nt_titus["resource_defs"] = {
  // some lines have been omitted

  nt_titus_commentary_by_nicoll: {
    collections_page_resource_desc: "ed. by W. R. Nicoll (1897)", 
    library_app_selectbox_title: "Commentary ed. by W. R. Nicoll (1897)",
    library_app_panel_title: "Commentary ed. by W. R. Nicoll (1897)",
    library_app_panel_subtitle: "",
    library_app_panel_text_from: "The Expositor's Greek Testament. Volume 4. Edited by W. R. Nicoll. 1897. London etc.: Hodder and Stoughton.",
    library_app_panel_note: "",
    scanned_or_typed: "scanned",
    resource_type: "commentary",
    scanned_source_shortname: "expositors_greek_testament_ed_nicoll_vol_4", 
    contents_shortname: "nt_titus_commentary_by_nicoll_contents"
  },

  // some lines have been omitted
}

After you add these lines, you should see this resource listed in Resources selectbox and in Collections page.

The key "collections_page_resource_desc" should have as its value a string "ed. by" plus author‚Äòs name and the year in brackets.

The key "library_app_panel_title" should have as its value the language plus "Commentary ed. by" or "Commentary by" plus author‚Äòs name and the year in brackets.

The key "library_app_panel_subtitle" should have as its value short subtitle of the resource. Here this key has empty string value because resource has no subtitle.

The key "library_app_panel_text_from" should have as its value bibliographic description of the book.

The key "library_app_panel_note" should have as its value some text. Most probably it will be some acknowledgments.

The key "scanned_or_typed" should have as its value the string "scanned".

The key "scanned_source_shortname" should have as its value the name of the directory (without path) in which has been uploaded the images of the pages of the book. Directory name includes short title of the book, string "ed" or "by" and name of the author.

The key "library_app_selectbox_title" should have as its value string "Commentary ed. by" or "Commentary by" then author's name and year in brackets.

The key "resource_type" should have the value "commentary".

The key "contents_shortname" should have as its value the name of the file containing resource's contents. The name of this file is usually formed by collection shortname plus resource type plus "by" plus author's name plus string "contents". Creating contents file and placing it in directory will be explaided below. [LINK TO BE ADDED]

Since classics text usually consists of several books and each book usually will have its own collection with its own commentary resource, the values of many keys will be repeated listing those commentary resources. In order to avoid repetitions it is recommended to define JSON object containing all keys whose values would be repeated. That JSON object should be the value of certain key of ParsedClassicsResProtos object which is in the file /data/_catalogues/_res_protos.js . Since the values of many keys will be repeated for all New Testament resources of the type "Commentary" based on volume 4 of the commentary by Nicoll, let's name the key "nt_commentary_by_nicoll_vol_4":

const ParsedClassicsResProtos = {
  // Commentary

  // some lines have been omitted

  nt_commentary_by_nicoll_vol_4: {
    collections_page_resource_desc: "ed. by W. R. Nicoll (1897)", 
    library_app_selectbox_title: "Commentary ed. by W. R. Nicoll (1897)",
    library_app_panel_title: "Commentary ed. by W. R. Nicoll (1897)",
    library_app_panel_subtitle: "",
    library_app_panel_text_from: "The Expositor's Greek Testament. Volume 4. Edited by W. R. Nicoll. 1897. London etc.: Hodder and Stoughton.",
    library_app_panel_note: "",
    scanned_or_typed: "scanned",
    resource_type: "commentary",
    scanned_source_shortname: "expositors_greek_testament_ed_nicoll_vol_4",
  },

  // some lines have been omitted
}

Now we can destructure the object ParsedClassicsCollProtos.nt_commentary_by_nicoll_vol_4 anywhere we need the same values of its keys:

ParsedClassicsCollDefs.nt_titus["resource_defs"] = {
  // some lines have been omitted

  nt_titus_commentary_by_nicoll: {
    ...ParsedClassicsResProtos.nt_commentary_by_nicoll_vol_4, 
    contents_shortname: "nt_titus_commentary_by_nicoll_contents"
  },

  // some lines have been omitted
}

Commentary references

Resource of the type "Commentary references" contains list of page numbers ‚Äì active links ‚Äì which lead into pages of collections of scholia or collections of extant fragments of ancient commentaries. That's specific content and it is quite possible, that there is simply no such collections of scholia or collections of extant fragments published for certain classics texts or there is only one or two. That means, that either there will not be possible to create resource of the type "Commentary references" or only one such resource will be created.

Resource of the type "Commentary references" will be transcribed.

As an example let‚Äòs list commentary references resource for Epistle to Titus collection. Todo it we need to add JSON object as the value of certain key of ParsedClassicsCollDefs.nt_titus["resource_defs"] object. In this case the key (resource shortname) is "nt_titus_commentary_refs_by_parsedclassics" (contains inside collection shortname, type of resource, string "by" and compilator's name):

ParsedClassicsCollDefs.nt_titus["resource_defs"] = {
  // some lines have been omitted

  // Commentary refs

  nt_titus_commentary_refs_by_parsedclassics: {
    collections_page_resource_desc: "compiled by ParsedClassics (2023)",
    library_app_selectbox_title: "Commentary references by ParsedClassics (2023)",
    library_app_panel_title: "Commentary references",
    library_app_panel_subtitle: "",
    library_app_panel_text_from: "",
    library_app_panel_note: "Compiled by ParsedClassics (2023)",
    scanned_or_typed: "typed",
    resource_type: "commentary_refs",
    scanned_source_shortname: "",
    contents_shortname: "",
  },

  // some lines have been omitted
}

After you add these lines, you should see this resource listed in Resources selectbox and in Collections page.

The key "collections_page_resource_desc" should have as its value a string "compiled by" plus author‚Äòs name and the year in brackets.

The key "library_app_panel_title" should have as its value "Commentary references".

The key "library_app_panel_subtitle" should have as its value short subtitle of the resource. Here this key has empty string value because resource has no subtitle.

The key "library_app_panel_text_from" should have as its value empty string.

The key "library_app_panel_note" should have as its value some text. Most probably it will be some acknowledgments.

The key "scanned_or_typed" should have as its value the string "typed".

The key "scanned_source_shortname" should have as its value empty string.

The key "library_app_selectbox_title" should have as its value string "Commentary references by" then compilator's name and year in brackets.

The key "resource_type" should have the value "commentary_refs".

The key "contents_shortname" should have as its value empty string.

Since classics text usually consists of several books and each book usually will have its own collection with its own commentary references resource, the values of many keys will be repeated listing those commentary references resources. In order to avoid repetitions it is recommended to define JSON object containing all keys whose values would be repeated. That JSON object should be the value of certain key of ParsedClassicsResProtos object which is in the file /data/_catalogues/_res_protos.js . Since the values of many keys will be repeated for all New Testament resources of the type "Commentary references", let's name the key "nt_commentary_refs_by_parsedclassics":

const ParsedClassicsResProtos = {
  // Commentary refs

  // some lines have been omitted

  nt_commentary_refs_by_parsedclassics: {
    collections_page_resource_desc: "compiled by ParsedClassics (2023)",
    library_app_selectbox_title: "Commentary references by ParsedClassics (2023)",
    library_app_panel_title: "Commentary references",
    library_app_panel_subtitle: "",
    library_app_panel_text_from: "",
    library_app_panel_note: "Compiled by ParsedClassics (2023)",
    scanned_or_typed: "typed",
    resource_type: "commentary_refs",
    scanned_source_shortname: "",
    contents_shortname: "",
  },

  // some lines have been omitted
}

Now we can destructure the object ParsedClassicsCollProtos.nt_commentary_refs_by_parsedclassics anywhere we need the same values of its keys:

ParsedClassicsCollDefs.nt_titus["resource_defs"] = {
  // some lines have been omitted

  // Commentary refs

  nt_titus_grammar_refs_by_parsedclassics: {
    ...ParsedClassicsResProtos.nt_grammar_refs_by_parsedclassics,
  },

  // some lines have been omitted

Grammar references

Resource of the type "Commentary references" contains list of page numbers ‚Äì active links ‚Äì which lead into pages of grammars. That's specific content and it is quite possible, that there is simply no grammars that have multiple references to certain classics text. That means, that either there will not be possible to create resource of the type "Grammar references" or only one such resource will be created in which all relevant grammars will be indexed.

Resource of the type "Grammar references" will be transcribed.

As an example let‚Äòs list grammar references resource for Epistle to Titus collection. Diagram set

There can be one diagram set resource in collection.

Resources of the type "Diagram set" are transcribed.

As an example let‚Äòs list diagram set resource for Epistle to Ephesians collection. The key "resource_type" should have the value "diagram_set".

Since classics text usually consists of several books and each book usually will have its own collection which may have its own diagram set resource, the values of many keys will be repeated listing those diagram set resources. In order to avoid repetitions it is recommended to define JSON object containing all keys whose values would be repeated. That JSON object should be the value of certain key of ParsedClassicsResProtos object which is in the file /data/_catalogues/_res_protos.js . const ParsedClassicsResProtos = {
  // some lines have been omitted  

  // Diagram set

  nt_diagrams_by_parsedclassics: {
    collections_page_resource_desc: "by ParsedClassics (2018)",

    library_app_panel_note: "",
    scanned_or_typed: "typed",
    resource_type: "diagram_set",
    scanned_source_shortname: "new_testament_in_original_greek_ed_robinson_pierpont", 
    contents_shortname: "",
  }, 

  // some lines have been omitted
}

Now we can destructure the object ParsedClassicsCollProtos.nt_diagrams_by_parsedclassics anywhere we need the same values of its keys:

ParsedClassicsCollDefs.nt_titus["resource_defs"] = {
  // some lines have been omitted

  // Diagram set

  nt_ephesians_diagrams_by_parsedclassics: {
    ...ParsedClassicsResProtos.nt_diagrams_by_parsedclassics,
  },

  // some lines have been omitted
}

Audio recording

There can be several audio recording resources in collection.

Resources of the type "Audio recording" are transcribed.

As an example let‚Äòs list commentary resource for Epistle to Titus collection. Todo it we need to add JSON object as the value of certain key of ParsedClassicsCollDefs.nt_titus["resource_defs"] object. In this case the key (resource shortname) is "nt_titus_audio_by_karvounakis" (contains inside collection shortname, type of resource, string "by" and author's name):

ParsedClassicsCollDefs.nt_titus["resource_defs"] = {
  // some lines have been omitted

  // Audio recording

  nt_titus_audio_by_karvounakis: {
    collections_page_resource_desc: "by Th. Karvounakis (2012)", 
    library_app_selectbox_title: "Audio recording by Th. Karvounakis (2012)",
    library_app_panel_title: "Audio recording by Th. Karvounakis",
    library_app_panel_subtitle: "",
    library_app_panel_text_from: "Novum Testamentum. Textus Stephanici A.D. 1550, cum variis lectionibus editionum Bezae, Elzeviri, Lachmanni, Tischendorfii, Tregellesii, Westcott-Hortii, versionis anglicanae emendatorum, curante F. H. A. Scrivener. 1887. Cantabrigiae: Deighton, Bell et soc.; Londini: Whittaker et soc.; G. Bell et filii.",
    library_app_panel_note: "Pronunciation: modern.",
    scanned_or_typed: "typed",
    resource_type: "audio_recording",
    scanned_source_shortname: "novum_testamentum_textus_stephanici_ed_scrivener",
    contents_shortname: "nt_titus_audio_by_karvounakis_contents",
  },

  // some lines have been omitted
}

After you add these lines, you should see this resource listed in Resources selectbox and in Collections page.

The key "collections_page_resource_desc" should have as its value a string "by" plus author‚Äòs name and the year in brackets.

The key "library_app_panel_title" should have as its value "Audio recording by" plus author‚Äòs name and the year in brackets.

The key "library_app_panel_subtitle" should have as its value short subtitle of the resource. Here this key has empty string value because resource has no subtitle.

The key "library_app_panel_text_from" should have as its value bibliographic description of the book.

The key "library_app_panel_note" should have as its value some text. Most probably it will be some acknowledgments.

The key "scanned_or_typed" should have as its value the string "typed".

The key "scanned_source_shortname" should have as its value the name of the directory (without path) in which have been uploaded the images of the pages of the book. Directory name includes short title of the book, string "ed" or "by" and name of the author.

The key "library_app_selectbox_title" should have as its value string "Audio recording by" then author's name and year in brackets.

The key "resource_type" should have the value "audio_recording".

The key "contents_shortname" should have as its value the name of the file containing resource's contents. The name of this file is usually formed by collection shortname plus resource type plus "by" plus author's name plus string "contents". Creating contents file and placing it in directory will be explained below. [LINK TO BE ADDED]

Since classics text usually consists of several books and each book usually will have its own collection with its own audio recording resource, the values of many keys will be repeated listing those audio recording resources. In order to avoid repetitions it is recommended to define JSON object containing all keys whose values would be repeated. That JSON object should be the value of certain key of ParsedClassicsResProtos object which is in the file /data/_catalogues/_res_protos.js . Since the values of mentioned keys will be repeated for all New Testament resources of the type "Audio recording" by Kervounakis, let's name the key "nt_audio_by_karvounakis":

const ParsedClassicsResProtos = {
  // some lines have been omitted  

  // Audio recording

  nt_audio_by_karvounakis: {
    collections_page_resource_desc: "by Th. Karvounakis (2012)", 
    library_app_selectbox_title: "Audio recording by Th. Karvounakis (2012)",
    library_app_panel_title: "Audio recording by Th. Karvounakis",
    library_app_panel_subtitle: "",
    library_app_panel_text_from: "Novum Testamentum. Textus Stephanici A.D. 1550, cum variis lectionibus editionum Bezae, Elzeviri, Lachmanni, Tischendorfii, Tregellesii, Westcott-Hortii, versionis anglicanae emendatorum, curante F. H. A. Scrivener. 1887. Cantabrigiae: Deighton, Bell et soc.; Londini: Whittaker et soc.; G. Bell et filii.",
    library_app_panel_note: "Pronunciation: modern.",
    scanned_or_typed: "typed",
    resource_type: "audio_recording",
    scanned_source_shortname: "novum_testamentum_textus_stephanici_ed_scrivener",
  }, 

  // some lines have been omitted
}

Now we can destructure the object ParsedClassicsCollProtos.nt_audio_by_karvounakis anywhere we need the same values of its keys:

ParsedClassicsCollDefs.nt_titus["resource_defs"] = {
  // some lines have been omitted

  // Audio recording

  nt_titus_audio_by_karvounakis: {
    ...ParsedClassicsResProtos.nt_audio_by_karvounakis,
    contents_shortname: "nt_titus_audio_by_karvounakis_contents",
  },

  // some lines have been omitted
}

Listing scanned books

All scanned resources and most transcribed resources have non empty value for the key "scanned_source_shortname" when are listed as part of some collection. The value of this key is a name of the directory (without path) in which have been uploaded the images of the pages of the book.

The book should also be listed. The senior editor should add a key to object ParsedClassicsScannedBooks in the file /data/_catalogues/_scanned_books.js and a JSON object as the value of that key. The key to object ParsedClassicsScannedBooks should be no other than the value of "scanned_source_shortname" we entered while listing resource.

Also there could be a need to list books which are referred to in resources of the type "Commentary references" or "Grammar references" (directories of the pages of such books are not entered as values of the key "scanned_source_shortname"). Listing of these books is done the same way.

For example, to list E. Robinson‚Äòs book Greek and English lexicon of the New Testament the key "greek_and_english_lexicon_of_nt_by_robinson" and JSON object as its value has been added to ParsedClassicsScannedBooks object:

ParsedClassicsScannedBooks = {

  // some lines have been omitted

  greek_and_english_lexicon_of_nt_by_robinson: {

    bookTitle: "A Greek and English lexicon of the New Testament."

    , bookUrlText: 'By Edward Robinson. Second edition. 1850. New York: Harper and Brothers.'

    , numLeafs: "816"

    , leafWidth: 1105

    , leafHeight: 1813

    , thumbnail: "page0001.jpg"

    , metadata: [

      {

      label: 'Title'

      , value: "A Greek and English lexicon of the New Testament. By Edward Robinson. Second edition. 1850. New York: Harper and Brothers."

      }

    ]

  }

  // some lines have been omitted

}

As you see the key "greek_and_english_lexicon_of_nt_by_robinson" includes at the beginning lowercase book title, the string "by", and lowercase author name at the end.

This key is used as directory name: /_scans/greek_and_english_lexicon_of_nt_by_robinson/ . This directory contains images of the pages of the scanned book.

The JSON object‚Äòs key "bookTitle" should have as its value scanned book title in book's language.

The key "bookUrlText" should have as its value all remaining bibliographic data of the book (author, edition, year, place, publishing house).

The key "numLeafs" should have as its value number of files in the directory containing images of the pages.

The key "leafWidth" should have as its value number of pixels of the width of scanned pages. This key is optional, but to add it is highly recommended because otherwise scanned pages might look slightly distorted.

The key "leafHeight" should have as its value number of pixels of the height of scanned pages. This key is optional, but to add it is highly recommended because otherwise scanned pages might look slightly distorted.

The key "thumbnail" should have as its value the filename of the image displaying the title page of the scanned book.

The key "label" should always have as its value the word "Title".

The key "value" should have as its value the string containing all relevant bibliographic data of the scanned book. Usually you will get it by combining values of the keys "bookTitle" and "bookUrlText".

Creating resources

Library app supports following types of resources: Parsed text, Original text, Concordance, Lexicon, Translation, Commentary, Commentary references, Grammar references, Diagram set, Audio recording. Parsed text, Commentary references, Grammar references, Diagram set, Audio recording resources can only be transcribed; Original text, Concordance, Lexicon, Translation, Commentary resources can be transcribed or scanned. Creating transcribed and scanned resources will be described separately because the process is very different.

Parsed text (transcribed)

Creating Parsed text resource involves creating two files: contents file and data file. The content file of the first listed Parsed text resource also serves as the content file for the whole collection.

Creating contents file

The contents file is being created by filling Parsed text contents generator form.

Let‚Äòs create contents file for parsed text resource we listed as part of Epistle to Titus collection.

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Contents shortname" should be the same as the value of the key "contents_shortname" we entered when we listed resource [LINK TO BE ADDED]. We entered for this key the value "nt_titus_parsed_text_contents", so we now should enter it as the value of the field.

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Line range" should be pipe delimited line ranges. In Epistle to Titus there are three chapters, the first having 16 verses, the second ‚Äì 15 verses and the third ‚Äì 15 verses. So, the value of this field should be 1-16|1-15|1-15 .

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Line number prefix" should be pipe delimited line prefixes, one for each chapter. Line number prefix usually indicates the chapter. The chapters of the New Testament are usually indicated by the number; colon usually used to separate chapter number from verse number. So, the value of this field should be 1:|2:|3: .

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Line index prefix" should be be pipe delimited line index prefixes, one for each chapter. Line index prefixes usually are the same line number prefixes. So, the value of this field eill be 1:|2:|3: .

After filling the fields the form should have the following look:

After filling fields with these values, click the button "Generate contents" and the contents code will be displayed in "Contents code output" textarea.

The code will be as this:

var nt_titus_parsed_text_contents = {

  "title": ""

  , "levelstart-1": ""

  , "1:1": "1:1"

  , "1:2": "1:2"

  // part of code has been cut out

  , "1:15": "1:15"

  , "1:16": "1:16"

  , "levelend-1": ""

  , "levelstart-2": ""

  , "2:1": "2:1"

  , "2:2": "2:2"

  // part of code has been cut out

  , "2:14": "2:14"

  , "2:15": "2:15"

  , "levelend-2": ""

  , "levelstart-3": ""

  , "3:1": "3:1"

  , "3:2": "3:2"

  // part of code has been cut out

  , "3:14": "3:14"

  , "3:15": "3:15"

  , "levelend-3": ""

};

Now let‚Äòs copy this code to code editor and let‚Äòs enter values for the keys "title" , "levelstart-1" , "levelstart-2", "levelstart-3". All these values should be in original language, in this case Greek. Since the key "title" is the index of the title, let‚Äòs enter "Œ§ŒØœÑŒªŒøœÇ" as the value of this key. Since the keys "levelstart-1" , "levelstart-2", "levelstart-3" are the indexes of the chapters, let‚Äòs enter "ŒöŒµœÜŒ¨ŒªŒ±ŒπŒøŒΩ A'", "ŒöŒµœÜŒ¨ŒªŒ±ŒπŒøŒΩ Œí'", "ŒöŒµœÜŒ¨ŒªŒ±ŒπŒøŒΩ Œì'" as the values of these keys.

After this the code will be as this:

var nt_titus_parsed_text_contents = {

  "title": "Œ§ŒØœÑŒªŒøœÇ"

  , "levelstart-1": "ŒöŒµœÜŒ¨ŒªŒ±ŒπŒøŒΩ A'"

  , "1:1": "1:1"

  , "1:2": "1:2"

  // part of code has been cut out

  , "1:15": "1:15"

  , "1:16": "1:16"

  , "levelend-1": ""

  , "levelstart-2": "ŒöŒµœÜŒ¨ŒªŒ±ŒπŒøŒΩ Œí'"

  , "2:1": "2:1"

  , "2:2": "2:2"

  // part of code has been cut out

  , "2:14": "2:14"

  , "2:15": "2:15"

  , "levelend-2": ""

  , "levelstart-3": "ŒöŒµœÜŒ¨ŒªŒ±ŒπŒøŒΩ Œì'"

  , "3:1": "3:1"

  , "3:2": "3:2"

  // part of code has been cut out

  , "3:14": "3:14"

  , "3:15": "3:15"

  , "levelend-3": ""

};

This code should be saved in the file having the same name as the value of the key "contents_shortname" which was entered when we listed [LINK TO BE ADDED] resource as part of collection. The value of the key "contents_shortname" is "nt_titus_parsed_text_contents", so the filename should be "nt_titus_parsed_text_contents.js". The file should be placed in directory which has the same name as resource shortname. The resource shortname is "nt_titus_parsed_text", so the direcrory to place contents file should be /data/parsed_text/nt_titus_parsed_text/ .

Creating data file

Data file‚Äòs name should be the same as resource shortname. The resource shortname is "nt_titus_parsed_text", so data file‚Äòs name should be "nt_titus_parsed_text.js". Data file should be placed in directory having the same name: /data/parsed_text/nt_titus_parsed_text/ .

Tags and required attributes

Data file uses certain formatting conventions.

HTML "span" tag having class attribute "line" should wrap each line of the text.

"span" tag having class attribute "line-number" should wrap verse number in each line. The same "span" element should also have attribute "data-line-number" whose value should be line number.

"span" tag having class attribute "word" should wrap each word. The same "span" element should also have the attributes "data-form", "data-part-of-speech", "data-parsing", "data-lemma". These four attributes contain morphological data of the word.

"span" tag having class attribute "para" should mark start of each new paragraph.

HTML code formatted using these "span" tags should be converted to string and made the value of javascript global variable whose name is the same as resource shortname.

This way we get such data file:

nt_titus_parsed_text =

`<span class="line"><span data-line-number="1:1" class="line-number">1:1</span>

<span class="word" data-form="·ΩÖ" data-part-of-speech="relative pronoun" data-parsing="accusative singular neuter" data-lemma="·ΩÖœÇ">·ΩÉ</span>

<span class="word" data-form="Œ∫Œ±œÑŒ¨" data-part-of-speech="preposition" data-parsing="" data-lemma="Œ∫Œ±œÑŒ¨">Œ∫Œ±œÑ‚Äô</span>

<span class="word" data-form="Œ∏ŒµŒø·ø¶" data-part-of-speech="noun" data-parsing="genitive singular masculine" data-lemma="Œ∏ŒµœåœÇ">Œ∏ŒµŒø·ø¶</span>, </span>`;

// part of code has been cut out
Optional attributes

It happens, that more than one word has the same lemma. E.g. in Greek-English lexicon to the New Testament by Th. S. Green two words have the lemma Œ¥Œ≠œâ, two words have the lemma ŒºŒÆŒΩ, and two words have the lemma ·ΩÖœÑŒπ. If one clicks in parsed text resource on the word whose lemma has more than one article in the dictionary, then by default the first article will be crolled into view.

In cases second, third etc. lexicon article should be loaded we need to use two additional attributes for the tag "span" having class "word". These are attributes "data-lexicon" and "data-lexicon-entry". The value of the attribute "data-lexicon" should be resource shortname of the relevant lexicon; the value of the attribute "data-lexicon-entry" should be order number of the entry which should be scrolled into view. E.g. the verse Matthew 9:38 contains the word Œ¥ŒµŒÆŒ∏Œ∑œÑŒµ, whose lemma is Œ¥Œ≠œâ. The needed article in Green's lexicon is second article for the lemma Œ¥Œ≠œâ. To load second article the code for the word Œ¥ŒµŒÆŒ∏Œ∑œÑŒµ in parsed text resource should be as this:

` <span class="word" data-form="δεŒÆθητε" data-part-of-speech="verb" data-parsing="aorist passive imperative 2nd person plural" data-lemma="δŒ≠ω" data-lexicon="greek_lexicon_to_nt_by_green" data-lexicon-entry="2">δεŒÆθητε</span>`

Parsing scheme

"span" tag having class attribute "word" should wrap each word in the data file. This "span" tag also has the attributes "data-form", "data-part-of-speech", "data-parsing", "data-lemma which contain morphological data of the word.

The attribute "data-form" contains as its value the same form of the word which "span" tag wraps. Usually the word wrapped and the value of "data-form" are exactly the same. But in some cases, as word undergoing elision or word having movable consonant or word having several orthographic variants the word wrapped and the value of "data-form" will be slightly different.

The attribute "data-lemma" contains as its value the dictionary lemma of the wrapped word.

The attribute "data-part-of-speech" contains as its value the name of the part of speech the wrapped word belongs to.

The attribute "data-parsing" contains as its value parsing data of the wrapped word except the part of speech.

The values of the attributes "data-part-of-speech" and "data-parsing" are entered according to parsing scheme. The attribute "data-part-of-speech" always must have a value and always contains one piece of data. The attribute "data-parsing" can be empty or contain one or more pieces of data. In case the attribute "data-parsing" contains several pieces of data, these pieces should be in proper order, i.e. each piece has its own position. E.g. the value of the attribute "data-parsing" for nouns should consist of case, number and gender exactly in this order.

The following table presents parsing scheme which is used to enter values for "data-part-of-speech" and "data-parsing" attributes:

Coding and parsing policy

Dealing with missing and differently numbered lines

It happens, that some lines of the classical text, which are included in some critical editions, are considered inauthentic and excluded from other editions. E.g. lines 16:25-27 of apostle Paul's epistle to Romans are included in Scrivener's edition, in Westcott and Hort's edition, and in Nestle and Nestle's edition of the New Testament, but are excluded from Robinson and Pierpont's edition and from Antoniadis's edition; in Westcott and Hort's edition and in Nestle and Nestle's edition of the New Testament the line 16:24 is not included.

So, it may be that the critical edition parsed text resource is based on lacks certain lines included in some other critical edition. In such case parsed text resource should include the line numbers of missing lines. In the parsed text of the apostle Paul's epistle to Romans which is based on Robinson and Pierpont's edition of the New Testament, the lines 16:25-27 are represented in parsed text resource's data file by their line numbers:

`<span class="line"><span data-line-number="16:25" class="line-number">16:25</span></span>


<span class="line"><span data-line-number="16:26" class="line-number">16:26</span></span>


<span class="line"><span data-line-number="16:27" class="line-number">16:27</span></span>`

After including numbers of missing lines in parsed text resource's data file we should not forget to to add these same lines into contents file.

Also it happens that some lines of the classical text are numbered slightly differently in some critical editions. E.g. the line from apostle John's Third Catholic epistle, which in Robinson and Pierpont's edition of the New Testament is numbered as 1:14, in Antoniadis's edition, in Scrivener's edition, in Westcott and Hort's edition and in Nestle and Nestle's edition is numbered as lines 1:14-15. In cases when numbering of lines has some differences across critical editions, it is best for parsed text to accept the most common numbering of lines.

Dealing with crasis

Cases of crasis, such as Œ∫·ºÄŒ∫Œµ·øñ, Œ∫·ºÄŒ∫Œµ·øñŒ∏ŒµŒΩ, Œ∫·ºÄŒ∫Œµ·øñŒΩŒøœÇ, Œ∫·ºÑŒΩ, œÑŒ±·ΩêœÑŒ¨, œÑŒø·ΩêŒΩŒ±ŒΩœÑŒØŒøŒΩ, œÑŒø·ΩîŒΩŒøŒºŒ±, œÑŒøœÖœÑŒ≠œÉœÑŒπ, although might be explained in certain dictionaries, should be treated as two words and those two words should be parsed separately. The "span" tag of the first word should contain that part of the crasis expression which is before vowel having breathing mark, and the "span" tag of the second word should contain part of the crasis expression strarting with vowel having breathing mark to the end of expression. E.g. in case of crasis expression Œ∫·ºÄŒ∫Œµ·øñŒ∏ŒµŒΩ the "span" tag of the first word will contain "Œ∫" and the "span" tag of the second word will contain "·ºÄŒ∫Œµ·øñŒ∏ŒµŒΩ". The code for crasis expression Œ∫·ºÄŒ∫Œµ·øñŒ∏ŒµŒΩ will be this:

`<span class="word" data-form="καŒØ" data-part-of-speech="conjunction" data-parsing="" data-lemma="καŒØ">κ</span><span class="word" data-form="·ºêκε·øñθεν" data-part-of-speech="adverb" data-parsing="" data-lemma="·ºêκε·øñθεν">·ºÄκε·øñθεν</span>`
Dealing with punctuation

Punctuation marks, i.e. symbols ",", ".", "¬∑", ";", "–", "—" should be outside "span" tag having class atribute "word", that is, "span" tag should not wrap the word together with punctuation symbol. E.g. in Matthew 2:10 there are punctuation marks "," and ".":

`<span class="line"><span data-line-number="2:10" class="line-number">2:10</span>
<span class="word" data-form="·º∞Œ¥œåŒΩœÑŒµœÇ" data-part-of-speech="verb" data-parsing="aorist active participle nominative plural masculine" data-lemma="·ΩÅœÅŒ¨œâ">·º∏Œ¥œåŒΩœÑŒµœÇ</span>
<span class="word" data-form="Œ¥Œ≠" data-part-of-speech="conjunction" data-parsing="" data-lemma="Œ¥Œ≠">Œ¥·Ω≤</span>
<span class="word" data-form="œÑœåŒΩ" data-part-of-speech="article" data-parsing="accusative singular masculine" data-lemma="·ΩÅ">œÑ·Ω∏ŒΩ</span>
<span class="word" data-form="·ºÄœÉœÑŒ≠œÅŒ±" data-part-of-speech="noun" data-parsing="accusative singular masculine" data-lemma="·ºÄœÉœÑŒÆœÅ">·ºÄœÉœÑŒ≠œÅŒ±</span>,
<span class="word" data-form="·ºêœáŒ¨œÅŒ∑œÉŒ±ŒΩ" data-part-of-speech="verb" data-parsing="aorist passive indicative 3rd person plural" data-lemma="œáŒ±ŒØœÅœâ">·ºêœáŒ¨œÅŒ∑œÉŒ±ŒΩ</span>
<span class="word" data-form="œáŒ±œÅŒ¨ŒΩ" data-part-of-speech="noun" data-parsing="accusative singular feminine" data-lemma="œáŒ±œÅŒ¨">œáŒ±œÅ·Ω∞ŒΩ</span>
<span class="word" data-form="ŒºŒµŒ≥Œ¨ŒªŒ∑ŒΩ" data-part-of-speech="adjective" data-parsing="accusative singular feminine" data-lemma="ŒºŒ≠Œ≥Œ±œÇ">ŒºŒµŒ≥Œ¨ŒªŒ∑ŒΩ</span>
<span class="word" data-form="œÉœÜœåŒ¥œÅŒ±" data-part-of-speech="adverb" data-parsing="" data-lemma="œÉœÜœåŒ¥œÅŒ±">œÉœÜœåŒ¥œÅŒ±</span>.' +
</span>`

The exception is apostroph symbol "‚Äô" marking elision. It should be inside "span" tag having class atribute "word", that is, "span" tag should wrap the word together with apostroph symbol. E.g. in Matthew 2:12 there are two apostroph symbols:

`<span class="line"><span data-line-number="2:12" class="line-number">2:12</span>

<span class="word" data-form="œáœÅŒ∑ŒºŒ±œÑŒπœÉŒ∏Œ≠ŒΩœÑŒµœÇ" data-part-of-speech="verb" data-parsing="aorist passive participle nominative plural masculine" data-lemma="œáœÅŒ∑ŒºŒ±œÑŒØŒ∂œâ">œáœÅŒ∑ŒºŒ±œÑŒπœÉŒ∏Œ≠ŒΩœÑŒµœÇ</span>
