Dealing with alternative characters

In unicode two or more code points may encode characters which look identically or have only stylistic difference. In order for all functionality to work correctly the uniformity of encoding must be enforced by using only characters from certain "standard" set. To achieve this go to Unicode Characters changer and use the form to change unicode characters into "standard" ones.

Original text (scanned)

In principle, resources belonging to type "Original text" can be either scanned or transcribed, but they surely will be all scanned because it is very difficult to reproduce complex formatting of the scholarly editions using very limitted means available in HTML. So, only creation of scanned resources of the type "Critical edition" will be described in Editor's documentation.

Creating image files

To create scanned resource of the type "Critical edition" you first need a series of JPG images, each image picturing one page of the book. Scanned resource always includes all pages of the book, i.e. each page from the title page to the last, not including covers and promotional materials. About creating a series of JPG files for scanned resource, read in Common tasks [LINK TO BE ADDED].

When you have a series of JPG files each image picturing one page of the book and named starting from page0001.jpg, submit them to the senior editor who will upload those files to the server. The files will be uploaded to the directory which was entered as value of the key "scanned_source_shortname" when original text resource was listed as part of collection. For example, in the Epistle to Titus collection the original text edited by V. Antoniadis has been listed [LINK TO BE ADDED] and the value of the key "scanned_source_shortname" is "kaine_diatheke_ed_antoniadis". It means that the pictures of the pages must be uploaded to the directory /_scans/kaine_diatheke_ed_antoniadis/ .

Having uploaded the images of the pages to the server, senior editor should list the scanned book as described in section Listing scanned books.

After uploading the files of the scanned book and listing it among scanned books, it can be browsed using the value of the key "scanned_source_shortname" in the URL: parsedclassics.com/reader/embedded_bookreader.html?kaine_diatheke_ed_antoniadis .

Creating contents file

In order for critical edition to work in sync with parsed text, the contents file must be created. To create contents file go to Scanned book contents generator page and fill the form:

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Line range" should be pipe delimited line ranges. In Epistle to Titus there are three chapters, the first having 16 verses, the second ‚Äì 15 verses and the third ‚Äì 15 verses. So, the value of this field should be 1-16|1-15|1-15 .

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Prefix" should be be pipe delimited line prefixes, one for each chapter. The chapters of the New Testament are usually indicated by the number written to the left from verse number; colon usually used to separate chapter number from verse number. So, the value for this field is 1:|2:|3: .

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Contents shortname" should be the same as the value of the key "contents_shortname" which was entered while listing resource as part of collection [LINK TO BE ADDED]. The value we entered for this key was "nt_titus_ed_antoniadis_contents", so we now should enter it as the value of the field "Contents shortname".

After filling fields with these values, click the button "Generate contents" and the contents code will be displayed in "Contents code output" textarea.

The code will be as this:

nt_titus_ed_antoniadis_contents = {

  "title": ""

  , "1:1": ""

  , "1:2": ""

  // part of code has been cut out

  , "1:15": ""

  , "1:16": ""

  , "2:1": ""

  , "2:2": ""

  // part of code has been cut out

  , "2:14": ""

  , "2:15": ""

  , "3:1": ""

  , "3:2": ""

  // part of code has been cut out

  , "3:14": ""

  , "3:15": ""

};

Now we need to enter values for each key of this JSON object. The keys are indexes of lines of the parsed text. "title" is the index of the title of the parsed text. The values should be numbers from image file names (without zero padding). View images of the scanned files, look for the numbers in their file names and enter those numbers as the values for relevant keys.

nt_titus_ed_antoniadis_contents = {
  
    "title": "451"
  
    , "1:1": "451"
  
    , "1:2": "451"
  
    // part of code has been cut out
  
    , "1:15": "451"
  
    , "1:16": "451"
  
    , "2:1": "452"
  
    , "2:2": "452"
  
    // part of code has been cut out
  
    , "2:14": "452"
  
    , "2:15": "452"
  
    , "3:1": "452"
  
    , "3:2": "452"
  
    // part of code has been cut out
  
    , "3:14": "453"
  
    , "3:15": "453"
  
  };

This code should be saved in the file having the same name as the value in "Contents shortname" field in the form, so it will be nt_titus_ed_antoniadis_contents.js . The file should be placed in directory whose name is the same ar resource shortname. Resource shortname is "nt_titus_text_ed_antoniadis" so the directory will be /data/original_text/nt_titus_text_ed_antoniadis/ .

After doing this critical edition resource should work in sync with parsed text resource.

Concordance (scanned)

Creating image files

To create scanned resource of the type "Concordance" you first need a series of JPG images, each image picturing one page of the book. Scanned resource always includes all pages of the book, i.e. each page from the title page to the last, not including covers and promotional materials. About creating a series of JPG files for scanned resource, read in Common tasks [LINK TO BE ADDED].

When you have a series of JPG files each image picturing one page of the book and named starting from page0001.jpg, submit them to the senior editor who will upload those files to the server. The files will be uploaded to the directory which was entered as value of the key "scanned_source_shortname" when concordance resource was listed as part of collection. For example, in the Epistle to Titus collection the concordance edited by W. F. Moulton and A. S. Geden has been listed [LINK TO BE ADDED] and the value of the key "scanned_source_shortname" is "concordance_to_greek_testament_by_moulton_geden". It means that the pictures of the pages must be uploaded to the directory /_scans/concordance_to_greek_testament_by_moulton_geden/ .

Having uploaded the images of the pages to the server, senior editor should list the scanned book as described in section Listing scanned books.

After uploading the files of the scanned book and listing it among scanned books, it can be browsed using the value of the key "scanned_source_shortname" in the URL: parsedclassics.com/reader/embedded_bookreader.html?concordance_to_greek_testament_by_moulton_geden .

In order for concordance to work in sync with parsed text, the contents file should be prepared. The same concordance resource can be listed as part of several collections. This means that there could be two cases: (1) there is no contents file and we need to create it; (2) there is contents file, but the words of certain classics book are not fully dealt with, so we need to supplement it.

Creating contents file

To create new contents file go to Word list generator page and fill the form:

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Language" should be "Greek" because in Epistle to Titus collection parsed text resource is in Greek.

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Parsed text code" should be full HTML code of the parsed text. Use browser‚Äôs HTML inspector (available on right-click in every major browser) to copy parsed text's HTML code from Library app‚Äôs page. To do this right-click inside HTML inspector's panel on the "div" element having "class" attribute "parsed-text-split-top" and in context menu select option "Copy outerHTML":

Then paste the copied string into form‚Äòs field. After that select and delete all code before first "span" tag having "class" attribute "line" and closing "div" tag from the code pasted into field:

After filling fields with these values, click the button "Load text" and the text will be displayed beneath "Parsed text:" heading.

After loading text click the button "Generate list" and the pipe delimited alphabetical list of all words in the text will appear in "Word list" textarea.

The word list will be as this:

·ºÄŒ≥Œ±Œ∏œåœÇ|·ºÄŒ≥Œ¨œÄŒ∑|·ºÖŒ≥ŒπŒøœÇ|·ºÅŒ≥ŒΩœåœÇ|·ºÄŒ¥ŒπŒ±œÜŒ∏ŒøœÅŒØŒ±|·ºÄŒ¥œåŒ∫ŒπŒºŒøœÇ|·ºÄŒµŒØ|Œ±·º±œÅŒµœÑŒπŒ∫œåœÇ|Œ±·º∞œÉœáœÅŒøŒ∫ŒµœÅŒ¥ŒÆœÇ|Œ±·º∞œÉœáœÅœåœÇ|Œ±·º∞œÑŒØŒ±|Œ±·º∞œéŒΩ|Œ±·º∞œéŒΩŒπŒøœÇ|·ºÑŒ∫Œ±œÅœÄŒøœÇ|·ºÄŒ∫Œ±œÑŒ¨Œ≥ŒΩœâœÉœÑŒøœÇ|·ºÄŒªŒÆŒ∏ŒµŒπŒ±|·ºÄŒªŒ∑Œ∏ŒÆœÇ|·ºÄŒªŒªŒ¨|·ºÄŒªŒªŒÆŒªœâŒΩ|·ºÅŒºŒ±œÅœÑŒ¨ŒΩœâ|·ºÑŒºŒ±œáŒøœÇ|·ºÄŒºŒÆŒΩ|·ºÄŒΩŒ±Œ≥Œ∫Œ±·øñŒøœÇ|·ºÄŒΩŒ±Œ∫Œ±ŒØŒΩœâœÉŒπœÇ|·ºÄŒΩŒ±œÑœÅŒ≠œÄœâ|·ºÄŒΩŒ≠Œ≥Œ∫ŒªŒ∑œÑŒøœÇ|·ºÄŒΩŒÆœÅ|·ºÑŒΩŒ∏œÅœâœÄŒøœÇ|·ºÄŒΩœåŒ∑œÑŒøœÇ|·ºÄŒΩŒøŒºŒØŒ±|·ºÄŒΩœÑŒ≠œáŒøŒºŒ±Œπ|·ºÄŒΩœÑŒπŒªŒ≠Œ≥œâ|·ºÄŒΩœÖœÄœåœÑŒ±Œ∫œÑŒøœÇ|·ºÄŒΩœâœÜŒµŒªŒÆœÇ|·ºÄœÄŒµŒπŒ∏ŒÆœÇ|·ºÑœÄŒπœÉœÑŒøœÇ|·ºÄœÄœå|·ºàœÄŒøŒªŒª·ø∂œÇ|·ºÄœÄœåœÉœÑŒøŒªŒøœÇ|·ºÄœÄŒøœÉœÑœÅŒ≠œÜœâ|·ºÄœÄŒøœÑœåŒºœâœÇ|·ºÄœÅŒ≥œåœÇ|·ºÄœÅŒΩŒ≠ŒøŒºŒ±Œπ|·ºàœÅœÑŒµŒº·æ∂œÇ|·ºÄœÅœáŒÆ|·ºÄœÉŒ≠Œ≤ŒµŒπŒ±|·ºÄœÉœÄŒ¨Œ∂ŒøŒºŒ±Œπ|·ºÄœÉœâœÑŒØŒ±|Œ±·ΩêŒ∏Œ¨Œ¥Œ∑œÇ|Œ±·ΩêœÑŒøŒ∫Œ±œÑŒ¨Œ∫œÅŒπœÑŒøœÇ|Œ±·ΩêœÑœåœÇ|·ºÄœÜŒ∏Œ±œÅœÉŒØŒ±|·ºÄœàŒµœÖŒ¥ŒÆœÇ|Œ≤Œ¥ŒµŒªœÖŒ∫œÑœåœÇ|Œ≤ŒªŒ±œÉœÜŒ∑ŒºŒ≠œâ|Œ≤ŒøœçŒªŒøŒºŒ±Œπ|Œ≥Œ¨œÅ|Œ≥Œ±œÉœÑŒÆœÅ|Œ≥ŒµŒΩŒµŒ±ŒªŒøŒ≥ŒØŒ±|Œ≥ŒØŒΩŒøŒºŒ±Œπ|Œ≥ŒΩŒÆœÉŒπŒøœÇ|Œ≥œÖŒΩŒÆ|Œ¥Œ≠|Œ¥ŒµœÉœÄœåœÑŒ∑œÇ|Œ¥ŒµœçœÑŒµœÅŒøœÇ|Œ¥Œ≠œâ|Œ¥ŒπŒ¨|Œ¥ŒπŒ±Œ≤ŒµŒ≤Œ±ŒπœåŒøŒºŒ±Œπ|Œ¥ŒπŒ¨Œ≤ŒøŒªŒøœÇ|Œ¥ŒπŒ¨Œ≥œâ|Œ¥ŒπŒ±œÑŒ¨œÉœÉœâ|Œ¥ŒπŒ¥Œ±œÉŒ∫Œ±ŒªŒØŒ±|Œ¥ŒπŒ¥Œ¨œÉŒ∫œâ|Œ¥ŒπŒ¥Œ±œáŒÆ|Œ¥ŒØŒ¥œâŒºŒπ|Œ¥ŒØŒ∫Œ±ŒπŒøœÇ|Œ¥ŒπŒ∫Œ±ŒπŒøœÉœçŒΩŒ∑|Œ¥ŒπŒ∫Œ±Œπœåœâ|Œ¥ŒπŒ∫Œ±ŒØœâœÇ|Œ¥œåŒæŒ±|Œ¥ŒøœÖŒªŒµœçœâ|Œ¥Œø·ø¶ŒªŒøœÇ|Œ¥ŒøœÖŒªœåœâ|Œ¥œÖŒΩŒ±œÑœåœÇ|·ºëŒ±œÖœÑŒø·ø¶|·ºêŒ≥Œ∫œÅŒ±œÑŒÆœÇ|·ºêŒ≥œé|Œµ·º∞|Œµ·º∞ŒºŒØ|Œµ·º∞œÅŒÆŒΩŒ∑|Œµ·º∑œÇ|Œµ·º∞œÇ|·ºêŒ∫|·ºêŒ∫Œµ·øñ|·ºêŒ∫Œµ·øñŒΩŒøœÇ|·ºêŒ∫ŒªŒµŒ∫œÑœåœÇ|·ºêŒ∫œÉœÑœÅŒ≠œÜŒøŒºŒ±Œπ|·ºêŒ∫œáŒ≠œâ|·ºêŒªŒ≠Œ≥œáœâ|·ºîŒªŒµŒøœÇ|·ºêŒªœÄŒØœÇ|·ºêŒΩ|·ºêŒΩŒ±ŒΩœÑŒØŒøœÇ|·ºêŒΩŒ¥ŒµŒØŒ∫ŒΩœÖŒºŒπ|·ºêŒΩœÑŒøŒªŒÆ|·ºêŒΩœÑœÅŒ≠œÄœâ|·ºêŒæŒøœÖœÉŒØŒ±|·ºêœÄŒ±Œ≥Œ≥Œ≠ŒªŒªŒøŒºŒ±Œπ|·ºêœÄŒØ|·ºêœÄŒØŒ≥ŒΩœâœÉŒπœÇ|·ºêœÄŒπŒ¥ŒπŒøœÅŒ∏œåœâ|·ºêœÄŒπŒµŒπŒ∫ŒÆœÇ|·ºêœÄŒπŒ∏œÖŒºŒØŒ±|·ºêœÄŒØœÉŒ∫ŒøœÄŒøœÇ|·ºêœÄŒπœÉœÑŒøŒºŒØŒ∂œâ|·ºêœÄŒπœÑŒ±Œ≥ŒÆ|·ºêœÄŒπœÜŒ±ŒØŒΩœâ|·ºêœÄŒπœÜŒ¨ŒΩŒµŒπŒ±|·ºîœÅŒ≥ŒøŒΩ|·ºîœÅŒπœÇ|·ºîœÅœáŒøŒºŒ±Œπ|·ºïœÑŒøŒπŒºŒøœÇ|Œµ·ΩêŒ¨œÅŒµœÉœÑŒøœÇ|Œµ·ΩêœÉŒ≠Œ≤ŒµŒπŒ±|Œµ·ΩêœÉŒµŒ≤·ø∂œÇ|·ºîœáœâ|Œ∂Œ¨œâ|Œ∂Œ∑ŒªœâœÑŒÆœÇ|ŒñŒ∑ŒΩ·æ∂œÇ|Œ∂ŒÆœÑŒ ÑŒπœÇ|Œ§ŒØœÑŒøœÇ|œÑŒøŒπŒø·ø¶œÑŒøœÇ|œÑœçœÄŒøœÇ|Œ§œÖœáŒπŒ∫œåœÇ|·ΩëŒ≥ŒπŒ±ŒØŒΩœâ|·ΩëŒ≥ŒπŒÆœÇ|·ΩëœÄŒ≠œÅ|·ΩëœÄŒøŒºŒπŒºŒΩ·øÑœÉŒ∫œâ|·ΩëœÄŒøŒºŒøŒΩŒÆ|·ΩëœÄŒøœÑŒ¨œÉœÉœâ|œÜŒ±ŒΩŒµœÅœåœâ|œÜŒ±·ø¶ŒªŒøœÇ|œÜŒ∏œåŒΩŒøœÇ|œÜŒπŒªŒ¨Œ≥Œ±Œ∏ŒøœÇ|œÜŒØŒªŒ±ŒΩŒ¥œÅŒøœÇ|œÜŒπŒªŒ±ŒΩŒ∏œÅœâœÄŒØŒ±|œÜŒπŒªŒ≠œâ|œÜŒπŒªœåŒæŒµŒΩŒøœÇ|œÜŒπŒªœåœÑŒµŒ∫ŒΩŒøœÇ|œÜœÅŒµŒΩŒ±œÄŒ¨œÑŒ∑œÇ|œÜœÅŒøŒΩœÑŒØŒ∂œâ|œáŒ¨œÅŒπŒΩ|œáŒ¨œÅŒπœÇ|œáœÅŒµŒØŒ±|œáœÅŒ∑œÉœÑœåœÑŒ∑œÇ|œáœÅŒπœÉœÑœåœÇ|œáœÅœåŒΩŒøœÇ|œàŒµœçœÉœÑŒ∑œÇ|·Ω°œÇ|·Ω°œÉŒ±œçœÑœâœÇ|·ΩÝœÜŒ≠ŒªŒπŒºŒøœÇ

Then click the button "Check for completeness". After this all words beneath the heading "Parsed text:" should be displayed on green backgound. If some words remain on white background, it means that the script was not able to generate complete list of words. Inform about it senior editor.

When you have pipe delimited alphabetical list of all words in the parsed text, go to Lexicon contents generator page and fill the form:

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Contents shortname" should be the same as the value of the key "contents_shortname" we entered when we listed resource [LINK TO BE ADDED]. We entered for this key the value "oncordance_to_greek_testament_by_moulton_geden_contents", so we now should enter it as the value of the field.

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Word list" should be just created pipe delimited alphabetical list of all words in the parsed text.

After filling fields with these values click the button "Generate contents" and the contents code will appear in "Contents code" textarea.

The contents code will be as this:

concordance_to_greek_testament_by_moulton_geden_contents = {

  /*Title page*/	"title": ""

  , /*·ºÄŒ≥Œ±Œ∏œåœÇ*/ "w-7936-947-945-952-972-962": ""

  , /*·ºÄŒ≥Œ¨œÄŒ∑*/ "w-7936-947-940-960-951": ""

  , /*·ºÖŒ≥ŒπŒøœÇ*/ "w-7941-947-953-959-962": ""

  , /*·ºÅŒ≥ŒΩœåœÇ*/ "w-7937-947-957-972-962": ""

  // part of code has been cut out

  , /*œáœÅŒπœÉœÑœåœÇ*/ "w-967-961-953-963-964-972-962": ""

  , /*œáœÅœåŒΩŒøœÇ*/ "w-967-961-972-957-959-962": ""

  , /*œàŒµœçœÉœÑŒ∑œÇ*/ "w-968-949-973-963-964-951-962": ""

  , /*·Ω°œÇ*/ "w-8033-962": ""

  , /*·Ω°œÉŒ±œçœÑœâœÇ*/ "w-8033-963-945-973-964-969-962": ""

  , /*·ΩÝœÜŒ≠ŒªŒπŒºŒøœÇ*/ "w-8032-966-941-955-953-956-959-962": ""

};

Now we need to enter values for each key of this JSON object. The keys are strings starting with "w" and consisting from numerical letter codes. "title" is the key for the title page of the concordane. The values should be numbers from image file names (without zero padding). View images of the scanned files, look for the numbers in their file names and enter those numbers as the values for relevant keys.

We get the following code:

concordance_to_greek_testament_by_moulton_geden_contents = {

  /*Title page*/	"title": "3"

  , /*·ºÄŒ≥Œ±Œ∏œåœÇ*/ "w-7936-947-945-952-972-962": "14"

  , /*·ºÄŒ≥Œ¨œÄŒ∑*/ "w-7936-947-940-960-951": "18"

  , /*·ºÖŒ≥ŒπŒøœÇ*/ "w-7941-947-953-959-962": "23"

  , /*·ºÅŒ≥ŒΩœåœÇ*/ "w-7937-947-957-972-962": "26"

  // part of code has been cut out

  , /*œáœÅŒπœÉœÑœåœÇ*/ "w-967-961-953-963-964-972-962": "1023"

  , /*œáœÅœåŒΩŒøœÇ*/ "w-967-961-972-957-959-962": "1030"

  , /*œàŒµœçœÉœÑŒ∑œÇ*/ "w-968-949-973-963-964-951-962": "1034"

  , /*·Ω°œÇ*/ "w-8033-962": "1038"

  , /*·Ω°œÉŒ±œçœÑœâœÇ*/ "w-8033-963-945-973-964-969-962": "1043"

  , /*·ΩÝœÜŒ≠ŒªŒπŒºŒøœÇ*/ "w-8032-966-941-955-953-956-959-962": "1044"

};

This code should be saved in the file having the same name as the value in "Contents shortname" field in the form. The file should be placed in directory whose name is the same ar resource shortname. Resource shortname is "concordance_by_moulton_geden" so the directory will be /data/concordance/concordance_by_moulton_geden/

After doing this Concordance resource should work in sync with parsed text resource.

Supplementing contents file

In case there is already contents file which contains words from one book of classics text, and we want that contents file would include also the words from other book of classics text, we need to supplement contents.

To do this go to Lexicon contents supplementer page and fill the form:

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Language" should be "Greek" because in Epistle to Titus collection parsed text resource is in Greek.

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Lexicon contents object" should be complete content of the concordance contents file. In previous section [LINK TO BE ADDED] we saved it as /data/concordance/concordance_by_moulton_geden/concordance_to_greek_testament_by_moulton_geden_contents.js .

The value of the form‚Äòs field "List of words to be added" should be pipe delimited alphabetical list of words contained in parsed text resource. How to create such word list has been described in previous section [LINK TO BE ADDED]. Here in this field we added list of words contained in parsed text resource from Epistle to Philemon collection.

After filling fields with these values, click the button "Load contents" and the code of the concordance contents object will be displayed beneath "Initial contents object:" heading.

Then click the button "Load words" and the list of words to be added to contents will be displayed beneath "Words to be added:" heading.

After that click the button "Add to contents" and the code of supplemented contents object will appear in "Supplemented contents code" textarea.

Then click the button "Check for completeness" and all words beneath the headings "Words to be added:" and "Initial contents object:" should be displayed in green background. If some words will not be displayed in green background, inform about it senior editor.

The code generated will be as this:

concordance_to_greek_testament_by_moulton_geden_contents = {

  /*Title page*/	"title": "3"

Notice, tat some keys have numerical values while the other keys have empty strings as their values. The latter represents the words which were not included in the initial contents object.

Now we need to enter numerical values for each key having empty string as its value. The values should be numbers from image file names (without zero padding). So, view images of the scanned files, look for the numbers in their file names and enter those numbers as the values for relevant keys.

We get the following code:

concordance_to_greek_testament_by_moulton_geden_contents = {

Replace with this code the contents of the file from which initial code was taken (in our case this was the file /data/concordance/concordance_by_moulton_geden/concordance_to_greek_testament_by_moulton_geden_contents.js) and save it.

After doing this concordance resource should work in sync with parsed text resource.

Workflows for multiple collections

Usually scanned resource of the type "Concordance" is being included into several collections. E.g. such resource as concordance edited by W. F. Moulton and A. S. Geden will be used in every collection dedicated to certain book of the New Testament. This means that the same contents file of the scanned resource of the type "Concordance" will be used by all relevant collections.

There are several workflows for creating contents file to be used by several collections.

Supplementing in stages

One possible workflow is as follows: at first we create new contents file to be used by certain single collection and fill the gaps with page numbers for all lemmas found in the parsed text of that collection. Then we supplement the contents file with the lemmas found in parsed text of another collection and fill the gaps with page numbers of these lemmas. And we repeat this process again and again until all lemmas of the all parsed texts of the all relevant collections are included in the contents file and all relevant page numbers are filled in.

This workflow has the advantage that we can work only with lemmas of the parsed text of the single collection and doing so quickly prepare one or more resources of the type "Concordance" to be used inside single collection. The disadvantage is that in each cycle we need again to browse through all pages of the scanned book in search for relevant lemmas and that takes a lot of time.

Supplementing at start

Another possible workflow is as follows: at first we create new contents file to be used by certain single collection. Then we don't fill the gaps with page numbers, but instead supplement the contents file with the lemmas found in original text of another collection. And we repeat this process again and again until all lemmas of the all original texts of the all relevant collections are included in the contents file. Then we browse through all pages of the scanned book, find the page numbers of the all lemmas and fill the gaps in contents file with these page numbers.

This workflow has the advantage that we must browse though all pages of the scanned book only once and this takes much less time than repeated browsing of the workflow described above. But the disadvantage is that we cannot work with the single collection at the time and must create huge contents file at once.

Cleaning page numbers

By using the first or the second workflow of those described above we get contents file of the resource of the type "Concordance" which is being used by multiple collections. We may need to add another resource of the type "Concordance" to the same collections. E.g. after having added concordance edited by W. F. Moulton and A. S. Geden to every collection dedicated to certain book of the New Testament we may need to add concordance edited by Ch. F. Hudson and E. Abbot to the same collections. In such cases we can shortcut the process by using the third workflow.

The contents file for the new resource of the type "Concordance" should contain the same lemmas. This means that we can reuse existing contents file: we only need to remove page numbers, to change the name of the contents object and to change the name of the file. To remove page numbers from the contents file use Lexicon page numbers cleaner. Copy contents object from the contents file, paste it in the field "Lexicon contents object" and click the button "Clean page numbers":

Then save the outputted contents object without page numbers using relevant variable name and file name.

Importing after cleaning

It may happen that one resource of the type "Concordance" has been added to multiple collections and another resource of the type "Concordance" has been added to just single or several collections. E.g. such resource as concordance edited by W. F. Moulton and A. S. Geden has been added to every collection dedicated to certain book of the New Testament, but such resource as concordance edited by Ch. F. Hudson and E. Abbot has been added to one or couple of collections. Now we need to add this resource to remaining collections.

In this case we need to use the following workflow. At first we should take that bigger contents file which contains comprehensive list of lemmas found in multiple collections and remove the page numbers from it. After that we need to import data into cleaned contents object from the contents object which contains less comprehensive list of lemmas from single collection or couple of collections. To do this go to Lexicon contents importer form and fill the fields:

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Language" should be "Greek" because lemmas in both contents objects are in Greek.

The value of the field "Lexicon contents object" should be contents object in which page numbers have been removed, i.e. that contents object which contains comprehensive list of lemmas found in multiple collections.

The value of the field "Lexicon contents object to be imported" should be contents object with all page numbers intact which contains less comprehensive list of lemmas from single collection or couple of collections.

After filling fields with such values click the button "Load contents" which is below the first textarea and the list of lemmas contained in the initial contents object will be displayed below the heading "Initial contents object:". Then click the button "Load contents" which is below the second textarea and the list of lemmas contained in contents object to be imported will be displayed below the heading "Contents object to be imported:". After that click the button "Import contents" and the resulting contents object will be outputted inside textarea "Resulting contents object code". Then click the button "Check for completeness". All lemmas below the headings "Contents object to be imported:" and "Initial contents object:" should be colored green. If certain lemmas remain not colored, inform about it senior editor.

Then save the resulting contents object using relevant object name and file name.

Concordance (transcribed)

Creating transcribed resource of the type "concordance" involves creating data file, contents file and target text files.

Creating data file

Let‚Äòs create data file of the transcribed concordance of the Epistle to Titus text.

The data file is being created by filling Concordance generator form:

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Language" should be "Greek" because in Epistle to Titus collection parsed text resource is in Greek.

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Book abbreviation" should be standard abbreviation of the title of the classical book. For example, abbreviation of the apostle Paul's First Epistle to Thessalonians would be "1 Thess.", abbreviation of the Revelation to John the Theologian would be "Rev.".

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Parsed text code" should be HTML code of the parsed text starting from the first "span" tag having class attribute value "line" and ending with the last "span" tag having the same class attribute value. Use browser‚Äôs HTML inspector [LINK TO BE ADDED] (available on right-click in every major browser) to copy this part of code from Library app‚Äôs page.

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Word list" should be pipe delimited alphabetical list of words contained in parsed text resource. How to create such word list has been described in the section on Creating contents file for scanned concordance resource.

After filling fields with these values, click the button "Load text" and the text will be displayed beneath "Parsed text:" heading.

After loading text click the button "Generate concordance" and the concordance code will appear in "Concordance code" textarea.

Then click the button "Check for completeness" and all words beneath the heading "Parsed text:" should be displayed in green background. If some words will not be displayed in green background, inform about it senior editor.

The generated concordance code will be as this:

Concordance HTML code should be converted to string and made the value of the variable having the same name as resource shortname. Transcribed concordance resource was listed [LINK TO BE ADDED] using "nt_conc_by_parsedclassics" as its shortname, so this will be variable name. To convert concordance HTML code to string it should be enclosed by the backtick/grave accent (` `) character.

This way we get such data file:

Data file‚Äòs name should be the same as resource shrtname. Transcribed concordance resource was listed [LINK TO BE ADDED] using "nt_conc_by_parsedclassics" as its shortname, so the filename will be "nt_conc_by_parsedclassics.js". Data file should be placed in directory also named after resource shortname: /data/concordance/nt_conc_by_parsedclassics/ .

After doing this concordance resource should work in sync with parsed text resource.

We compiled grammatical concordance just for one book. In some cases this might be enough, but usually concordance compiled just for one book is not very useful. Much more useful would be to compile concordance for all books of certain classical text or to compile concordance for all texts written by certain author. We can compile concordance for several books by using Concordance supplementer form:

Let's say we want to compile grammatical concordance for all books of the New Testament starting from Gospel according to Matthew and ending with Revelation to John the Theologian. To achieve this we at first need to supplement concordance of the Gospel according to Matthew with the concordance of the Gospel according to Mark, then the resulting concordance we should supplement with the concordance of the Gospel according to Luke etc. until we reach the last book of the New Testament, the Revelation to John the Theologian.

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Language" should be "Greek" because New Testament is in Greek.

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Concordance to be supplemented" should be the code of the concordance of the Gospel according to Matthew.

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Concordance to be supplemented" should be the code of the concordance of the Gospel according to Mark.

Having filled form's fields with these values, we should load both concordances by clicking "Load concordance" buttons and then we should click the button "Supplement concordance". The code of resulting concordance will be outputted in "Concordance code" textarea and resulting concordance will be displayed under "Concordance supplemented:" heading. Now we can click "Check for completeness" button to see if everything which was included in concordance to be supplemented and in concordance to be added is also included in resulting concordance. All words and line numbers of the concordance to be supplemented and of the concordance to be added should become green. If any word or line number became red and is included in square brackets (symbols []), inform about it senior editor.

Now that we have grammatical concordance of the Gospels according to Matthew and Mark, let's copy its code and paste it in the field "Concordance to be supplemented", then let's paste the code of the concordance of the Gospel according to Luke in the field "Concordance to be added". After clicking button "Supplement concordance" we will have concordance which includes words of these three books. We can repeat this process until we compile concordance for all 27 books of the New Testament. The resulting concordance code should be converted to string and be made the value of the variable "nt_conc_by_parsedclassics" as has been described above.

The code resulting should be saved in the file named as the variable i.e. "nt_conc_by_parsedclassics.js". The file should be placed in directory /data/concordance/nt_conc_by_parsedclassics/ .

Creating contents file

Concordance data file includes for each word form the list book abbreviations together with line numbers indicating places where the word form is present. Clicking the line number should open the original text in exact place. To enable this functionality we need to add contents file.

Let's create contents file for concordance containing words of all 27 New Testament's books. The name of the contents file should be formed by adding "contents" to the end of the data file's name, and this way we get file name "nt_conc_by_parsedclassics_contents.js".

The code inside the file "nt_conc_by_parsedclassics_contents.js" will be as follows:

nt_conc_by_parsedclassics_contents = {

  "Matt.": "nt_conc_by_parsedclassics_matthew_parsed_text",
  "Mark": "nt_conc_by_parsedclassics_mark_parsed_text",

  "1 John": "nt_conc_by_parsedclassics_john_1_parsed_text",

      },
      
      // part of code has been cut out
      
      "nt_conc_by_parsedclassics_revelation_parsed_text": {
        "author_orig": "·º© ŒöŒ±ŒπŒΩ·Ω¥ ŒîŒπŒ±Œ∏ŒÆŒ∫Œ∑",
        "library_app_panel_text_from": "The New Testament in the original Greek. Byzantine textform. Compiled and arranged by M. A. Robinson and W. G. Pierpont. 2005. Southborough, MA: Chilton book publishing.",
        "scanned_source_shortname": "new_testament_in_original_greek_ed_robinson_pierpont",
        "library_app_panel_note": "",
        "library_app_panel_title": "·ºàœÄŒøŒ∫·Ω±ŒªœÖœàŒπœÇ ·º∏œâ·Ω±ŒΩŒΩŒøœÖ œÑŒø·ø¶ Œ∏ŒµŒøŒª·ΩπŒ≥ŒøœÖ"
      }

  }

};

This code initializes global variable "nt_conc_by_parsedclassics_contents", which as you see has the same name as the file. The value of this variable is JSON object. The keys of this object are abbreviations of the titles of the New Testament books and the values of these keys are strings which refer to files containing parsed text of relevant New Testament books. There are also the key "titles" whose value is an JSON object having as its keys just mentioned strings. The values of these keys are JSON objects having several keys: "author_orig", "library_app_panel_text_from", "scanned_source_shortname", "library_app_panel_note", "library_app_panel_title". These keys together with their values should be copied from the files which contain relevant collection and resource definitions, i.e. from files _collections.js and _res_protos.js from /data/catalogues/ directory.

As you can see, the keys of the object nt_conc_by_parsedclassics_contents.titles have many common values. To avoid the repetitios we can desctructure relevant objects from _collections.js and _res_protos.js files. The code would be as follows:

nt_conc_by_parsedclassics_contents = {

  "Matt.": "nt_conc_by_parsedclassics_matthew_parsed_text",
  "Mark": "nt_conc_by_parsedclassics_mark_parsed_text",

    "nt_conc_by_parsedclassics_matthew_parsed_text": {

    },

    // part of code has been cut out

    }

  }

Now put the file "nt_conc_by_parsedclassics_contents.js" to the directory /data/concordance/nt_conc_by_parsedclassics/ .

Creating target text files

Contents file we just created is the link between concordance and original text. Clicking on line numbers in concordance (rendered by data file) should display the original text (rendered by target text file) at exact place. One target file contains one book of classics text, so, since classics text usually consists of several books, most often there will be a need to create several target text files.

For New Testament corcondance we need to create 27 target text files. Their names will be the strings from contents file which are values of abbreviations of the titles of the New Testament books. E.g. abbreviation "Titus" as a key has as its value the string "nt_conc_by_parsedclassics_titus_parsed_text", so the file name will be "nt_conc_by_parsedclassics_titus_parsed_text.js".

Inside this file there should be the variable of the same name and its value should be the string containing parsed text of the relevant book. Parsed text can be taken from data file of relevant parsed text resource.

The code would be as this:

Lexicon (scanned)

Creating image files

To create scanned resource of the type "Lexicon" you first need a series of JPG images, each image picturing one page of the book. Scanned resource always includes all pages of the book, i.e. each page from the title page to the last, not including covers and promotional materials. About creating a series of JPG files for scanned resource, read in Common tasks [LINK TO BE ADDED].

When you have a series of JPG files each image picturing one page of the book and named starting from page0001.jpg, submit them to the senior editor who will upload those files to the server. The files will be uploaded to the directory which was entered as value of the key "scanned_source_shortname" when lexicon resource was listed as part of collection. For example, in the Epistle to Titus collection the lexicon by E. Robinson has been listed [LINK TO BE ADDED] and the value of the key "scanned_source_shortname" is "greek_and_english_lexicon_of_nt_by_robinson". It means that the pictures of the pages must be uploaded to the directory /_scans/greek_and_english_lexicon_of_nt_by_robinson/ .

Having uploaded the images of the pages to the server, senior editor should list the scanned book as described in section Listing scanned books.

After uploading the files of the scanned book and listing it among scanned books, it can be browsed using the value of the key "scanned_source_shortname" in the URL: parsedclassics.com/reader/embedded_bookreader.html?greek_and_english_lexicon_of_nt_by_robinson .

In order for lexicon to work in sync with parsed text, the contents file should be prepared. The same lexicon resource can be listed as part of several collections. This means that there could be two cases: (1) there is no contents file and we need to create it; (2) there is contents file, but the words of certain classics book are not fully dealt with, so we need to supplement it.

Creating contents file

To create new contents file go to Word list generator page and fill the form:

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Language" should be "Greek" because in Epistle to Titus collection parsed text resource is in Greek.

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Parsed text code" should be full HTML code of the parsed text. Use browser‚Äôs HTML inspector (available on right-click in every major browser) to copy parsed text's HTML code from Library app‚Äôs page. To do this right-click inside HTML inspector's panel on the "div" element having "class" attribute "parsed-text-split-top" and in context menu select option "Copy outerHTML":

Then paste the copied string into form‚Äòs field. After that select and delete all code before first "span" tag having "class" attribute "line" and closing "div" tag from the code pasted into field:

After filling fields with these values, click the button "Load text" and the text will be displayed beneath "Parsed text:" heading.

After loading text click the button "Generate list" and the pipe delimited alphabetical list of all words in the text will appear in "Word list" textarea.

The word list will be as this:

·ºÄŒ≥Œ±Œ∏œåœÇ|·ºÄŒ≥Œ¨œÄŒ∑|·ºÖŒ≥ŒπŒøœÇ|·ºÅŒ≥ŒΩœåœÇ|·ºÄŒ¥ŒπŒ±œÜŒ∏ŒøœÅŒØŒ±|·ºÄŒ¥œåŒ∫ŒπŒºŒøœÇ|·ºÄŒµŒØ|Œ±·º±œÅŒµœÑŒπŒ∫œåœÇ|Œ±·º∞œÉœáœÅŒøŒ∫ŒµœÅŒ¥ŒÆœÇ|Œ±·º∞œÉœáœÅœåœÇ|Œ±·º∞œÑŒØŒ±|Œ±·º∞œéŒΩ|Œ±·º∞œéŒΩŒπŒøœÇ|·ºÑŒ∫Œ±œÅœÄŒøœÇ|·ºÄŒ∫Œ±œÑŒ¨Œ≥ŒΩœâœÉœÑŒøœÇ|·ºÄŒªŒÆŒ∏ŒµŒπŒ±|·ºÄŒªŒ∑Œ∏ŒÆœÇ|·ºÄŒªŒªŒ¨|·ºÄŒªŒªŒÆŒªœâŒΩ|·ºÅŒºŒ±œÅœÑŒ¨ŒΩœâ|·ºÑŒºŒ±œáŒøœÇ|·ºÄŒºŒÆŒΩ|·ºÄŒΩŒ±Œ≥Œ∫Œ±·øñŒøœÇ|·ºÄŒΩŒ±Œ∫Œ±ŒØŒΩœâœÉŒπœÇ|·ºÄŒΩŒ±œÑœÅŒ≠œÄœâ|·ºÄŒΩŒ≠Œ≥Œ∫ŒªŒ∑œÑŒøœÇ|·ºÄŒΩŒÆœÅ|·ºÑŒΩŒ∏œÅœâœÄŒøœÇ|·ºÄŒΩœåŒ∑œÑŒøœÇ|·ºÄŒΩŒøŒºŒØŒ±|·ºÄŒΩœÑŒ≠œáŒøŒºŒ±Œπ|·ºÄŒΩœÑŒπŒªŒ≠Œ≥œâ|·ºÄŒΩœÖœÄœåœÑŒ±Œ∫œÑŒøœÇ|·ºÄŒΩœâœÜŒµŒªŒÆœÇ|·ºÄœÄŒµŒπŒ∏ŒÆœÇ|·ºÑœÄŒπœÉœÑŒøœÇ|·ºÄœÄœå|·ºàœÄŒøŒªŒª·ø∂œÇ|·ºÄœÄœåœÉœÑŒøŒªŒøœÇ|·ºÄœÄŒøœÉœÑœÅŒ≠œÜœâ|·ºÄœÄŒøœÑœåŒºœâœÇ|·ºÄœÅŒ≥œåœÇ|·ºÄœÅŒΩŒ≠ŒøŒºŒ±Œπ|·ºàœÅœÑŒµŒº·æ∂œÇ|·ºÄœÅœáŒÆ|·ºÄœÉŒ≠Œ≤ŒµŒπŒ±|·ºÄœÉœÄŒ¨Œ∂ŒøŒºŒ±Œπ|·ºÄœÉœâœÑŒØŒ±|Œ±·ΩêŒ∏Œ¨Œ¥Œ∑œÇ|Œ±·ΩêœÑŒøŒ∫Œ±œÑŒ¨Œ∫œÅŒπœÑŒøœÇ|Œ±·ΩêœÑœåœÇ|·ºÄœÜŒ∏Œ±œÅœÉŒØŒ±|·ºÄœàŒµœÖŒ¥ŒÆœÇ|Œ≤Œ¥ŒµŒªœÖŒ∫œÑœåœÇ|Œ≤ŒªŒ±œÉœÜŒ∑ŒºŒ≠œâ|Œ≤ŒøœçŒªŒøŒºŒ±Œπ|Œ≥Œ¨œÅ|Œ≥Œ±œÉœÑŒÆœÅ|Œ≥ŒµŒΩŒµŒ±ŒªŒøŒ≥ŒØŒ±|Œ≥ŒØŒΩŒøŒºŒ±Œπ|Œ≥ŒΩŒÆœÉŒπŒøœÇ|Œ≥œÖŒΩŒÆ|Œ¥Œ≠|Œ¥ŒµœÉœÄœåœÑŒ∑œÇ|Œ¥ŒµœçœÑŒµœÅŒøœÇ|Œ¥Œ≠œâ|Œ¥ŒπŒ¨|Œ¥ŒπŒ±Œ≤ŒµŒ≤Œ±ŒπœåŒøŒºŒ±Œπ|Œ¥ŒπŒ¨Œ≤ŒøŒªŒøœÇ|Œ¥ŒπŒ¨Œ≥œâ|Œ¥ŒπŒ±œÑŒ¨œÉœÉœâ|Œ¥ŒπŒ¥Œ±œÉŒ∫Œ±ŒªŒØŒ±|Œ¥ŒπŒ¥Œ¨œÉŒ∫œâ|Œ¥ŒπŒ¥Œ±œáŒÆ|Œ¥ŒØŒ¥œâŒºŒπ|Œ¥ŒØŒ∫Œ±ŒπŒøœÇ|Œ¥ŒπŒ∫Œ±ŒπŒøœÉœçŒΩŒ∑|Œ¥ŒπŒ∫Œ±Œπœåœâ|Œ¥ŒπŒ∫Œ±ŒØœâœÇ|Œ¥œåŒæŒ±|Œ¥ŒøœÖŒªŒµœçœâ|Œ¥Œø·ø¶ŒªŒøœÇ|Œ¥ŒøœÖŒªœåœâ|Œ¥œÖŒΩŒ±œÑœåœÇ|·ºëŒ±œÖœÑŒø·ø¶|·ºêŒ≥Œ∫œÅŒ±œÑŒÆœÇ|·ºêŒ≥œé|Œµ·º∞|Œµ·º∞ŒºŒØ|Œµ·º∞œÅŒÆŒΩŒ∑|Œµ·º∑œÇ|Œµ·º∞œÇ|·ºêŒ∫|·ºêŒ∫Œµ·øñ|·ºêŒ∫Œµ·øñŒΩŒøœÇ|·ºêŒ∫ŒªŒµŒ∫œÑœåœÇ|·ºêŒ∫œÉœÑœÅŒ≠œÜŒøŒºŒ±Œπ|·ºêŒ∫œáŒ≠œâ|·ºêŒªŒ≠Œ≥œáœâ|·ºîŒªŒµŒøœÇ|·ºêŒªœÄŒØœÇ|·ºêŒΩ|·ºêŒΩŒ±ŒΩœÑŒØŒøœÇ|·ºêŒΩŒ¥ŒµŒØŒ∫ŒΩœÖŒºŒπ|·ºêŒΩœÑŒøŒªŒÆ|·ºêŒΩœÑœÅŒ≠œÄœâ|·ºêŒæŒøœÖœÉŒØŒ±|·ºêœÄŒ±Œ≥Œ≥Œ≠ŒªŒªŒøŒºŒ±Œπ|·ºêœÄŒØ|·ºêœÄŒØŒ≥ŒΩœâœÉŒπœÇ|·ºêœÄŒπŒ¥ŒπŒøœÅŒ∏œåœâ|·ºêœÄŒπŒµŒπŒ∫ŒÆœÇ|·ºêœÄŒπŒ∏œÖŒºŒØŒ±|·ºêœÄŒØœÉŒ∫ŒøœÄŒøœÇ|·ºêœÄŒπœÉœÑŒøŒºŒØŒ∂œâ|·ºêœÄŒπœÑŒ±Œ≥ŒÆ|·ºêœÄŒπœÜŒ±ŒØŒΩœâ|·ºêœÄŒπœÜŒ¨ŒΩŒµŒπŒ±|·ºîœÅŒ≥ŒøŒΩ|·ºîœÅŒπœÇ|·ºîœÅœáŒøŒºŒ±Œπ|·ºïœÑŒøŒπŒºŒøœÇ|Œµ·ΩêŒ¨œÅŒµœÉœÑŒøœÇ|Œµ·ΩêœÉŒ≠Œ≤ŒµŒπŒ±|Œµ·ΩêœÉŒµŒ≤·ø∂œÇ|·ºîœáœâ|Œ∂Œ¨œâ|Œ∂Œ∑ŒªœâœÑŒÆœÇ|ŒñŒ∑ŒΩ·æ∂œÇ|Œ∂ŒÆœÑŒ ÑŒπœÇ|Œ§ŒØœÑŒøœÇ|œÑŒøŒπŒø·ø¶œÑŒøœÇ|œÑœçœÄŒøœÇ|Œ§œÖœáŒπŒ∫œåœÇ|·ΩëŒ≥ŒπŒ±ŒØŒΩœâ|·ΩëŒ≥ŒπŒÆœÇ|·ΩëœÄŒ≠œÅ|·ΩëœÄŒøŒºŒπŒºŒΩ·øÑœÉŒ∫œâ|·ΩëœÄŒøŒºŒøŒΩŒÆ|·ΩëœÄŒøœÑŒ¨œÉœÉœâ|œÜŒ±ŒΩŒµœÅœåœâ|œÜŒ±·ø¶ŒªŒøœÇ|œÜŒ∏œåŒΩŒøœÇ|œÜŒπŒªŒ¨Œ≥Œ±Œ∏ŒøœÇ|œÜŒØŒªŒ±ŒΩŒ¥œÅŒøœÇ|œÜŒπŒªŒ±ŒΩŒ∏œÅœâœÄŒØŒ±|œÜŒπŒªŒ≠œâ|œÜŒπŒªœåŒæŒµŒΩŒøœÇ|œÜŒπŒªœåœÑŒµŒ∫ŒΩŒøœÇ|œÜœÅŒµŒΩŒ±œÄŒ¨œÑŒ∑œÇ|œÜœÅŒøŒΩœÑŒØŒ∂œâ|œáŒ¨œÅŒπŒΩ|œáŒ¨œÅŒπœÇ|œáœÅŒµŒØŒ±|œáœÅŒ∑œÉœÑœåœÑŒ∑œÇ|œáœÅŒπœÉœÑœåœÇ|œáœÅœåŒΩŒøœÇ|œàŒµœçœÉœÑŒ∑œÇ|·Ω°œÇ|·Ω°œÉŒ±œçœÑœâœÇ|·ΩÝœÜŒ≠ŒªŒπŒºŒøœÇ

Then click the button "Check for completeness". After this all words beneath the heading "Parsed text:" should be displayed on green backgound. If some words remain on white background, it means that the script was not able to generate complete list of words. Inform about it senior editor.

When you have pipe delimited alphabetical list of all words in the parsed text, go to Lexicon contents generator page and fill the form:

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Contents shortname" should be the same as the value of the key "contents_shortname" we entered when we listed resource [LINK TO BE ADDED]. We entered for this key the value "greek_and_english_lexicon_of_nt_by_robinson_contents", so we now should enter it as the value of the field.

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Word list" should be just created pipe delimited alphabetical list of all words in the parsed text.

After filling fields with these values click the button "Generate contents" and the contents code will appear in "Contents code" textarea.

The contents code will be as this:

greek_and_english_lexicon_of_nt_by_robinson_contents = {

  /*Title page*/	"title": ""

  , /*·ºÄŒ≥Œ±Œ∏œåœÇ*/ "w-7936-947-945-952-972-962": ""

  , /*·ºÄŒ≥Œ¨œÄŒ∑*/ "w-7936-947-940-960-951": ""

  , /*·ºÖŒ≥ŒπŒøœÇ*/ "w-7941-947-953-959-962": ""

  , /*·ºÅŒ≥ŒΩœåœÇ*/ "w-7937-947-957-972-962": ""

  // part of code has been cut out

  , /*œáœÅŒπœÉœÑœåœÇ*/ "w-967-961-953-963-964-972-962": ""

  , /*œáœÅœåŒΩŒøœÇ*/ "w-967-961-972-957-959-962": ""

  , /*œàŒµœçœÉœÑŒ∑œÇ*/ "w-968-949-973-963-964-951-962": ""

  , /*·Ω°œÇ*/ "w-8033-962": ""

  , /*·Ω°œÉŒ±œçœÑœâœÇ*/ "w-8033-963-945-973-964-969-962": ""

  , /*·ΩÝœÜŒ≠ŒªŒπŒºŒøœÇ*/ "w-8032-966-941-955-953-956-959-962": ""

};

Now we need to enter values for each key of this JSON object. The keys are strings starting with "w" and consisting from numerical letter codes. "title" is the key for the title page of the lexicon. The values should be numbers from image file names (without zero padding). View images of the scanned files, look for the numbers in their file names and enter those numbers as the values for relevant keys.

We get the following code:

greek_and_english_lexicon_of_nt_by_robinson_contents = {

  /*Title page*/	"title": ""

  , /*·ºÄŒ≥Œ±Œ∏œåœÇ*/ "w-7936-947-945-952-972-962": "15"

  , /*·ºÄŒ≥Œ¨œÄŒ∑*/ "w-7936-947-940-960-951": "17"

  , /*·ºÖŒ≥ŒπŒøœÇ*/ "w-7941-947-953-959-962": "19"

  , /*·ºÅŒ≥ŒΩœåœÇ*/ "w-7937-947-957-972-962": "21"

  // part of code has been cut out

  , /*œáœÅŒπœÉœÑœåœÇ*/ "w-967-961-953-963-964-972-962": "799"

  , /*œáœÅœåŒΩŒøœÇ*/ "w-967-961-972-957-959-962": "800"

  , /*œàŒµœçœÉœÑŒ∑œÇ*/ "w-968-949-973-963-964-951-962": "804"

  , /*·Ω°œÇ*/ "w-8033-962": "810"

  , /*·Ω°œÉŒ±œçœÑœâœÇ*/ "w-8033-963-945-973-964-969-962": "813"

  , /*·ΩÝœÜŒ≠ŒªŒπŒºŒøœÇ*/ "w-8032-966-941-955-953-956-959-962": "815"

};

This code should be saved in the file having the same name as the value in "Contents shortname" field in the form. The file should be placed in directory whose name is the same ar resource shortname. Resource shortname is "greek_lexicon_of_nt_by_robinson" so the directory will be /data/lexicon/greek_lexicon_of_nt_by_robinson/ .

After doing this lexicon resource should work in sync with parsed text resource.

Supplementing contents file

In case there is already contents file which contains words from one book of classics text, and we want that contents file would include also the words from other book of classics text, we need to supplement contents.

To do this go to Lexicon contents supplementer page and fill the form:

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Language" should be "Greek" because in Epistle to Titus collection parsed text resource is in Greek.

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Lexicon contents object" should be complete content of the lexicon contents file. In previous section [LINK TO BE ADDED] we saved it as /data/lexicon/greek_lexicon_of_nt_by_robinson/greek_and_english_lexicon_of_nt_by_robinson_contents.js .

The value of the form‚Äòs field "List of words to be added" should be pipe delimited alphabetical list of words contained in parsed text resource. How to create such word list has been described in previous section [LINK TO BE ADDED]. Here in this field we added list of words contained in parsed text resource from Epistle to Philemon collection.

After filling fields with these values, click the button "Load contents" and the code of the concordance contents object will be displayed beneath "Initial contents object:" heading.

Then click the button "Load words" and the list of words to be added to contents will be displayed beneath "Words to be added:" heading.

After that click the button "Add to contents" and the code of supplemented contents object will appear in "Supplemented contents code" textarea.

Then click the button "Check for completeness" and all words beneath the headings "Words to be added:" and "Initial contents object:" should be displayed in green background. If some words will not be displayed in green background, inform about it senior editor.

The code generated will be as this:

greek_and_english_lexicon_of_nt_by_robinson_contents = {

  /*Title page*/	"title": "3"

  , /*·ºÄŒ≥Œ±Œ∏œåœÇ*/ "w-7936-947-945-952-972-962": "14"

  , /*·ºÄŒ≥Œ¨œÄŒ∑*/ "w-7936-947-940-960-951": "18"

Notice, tat some keys have numerical values while the other keys have empty strings as their values. The latter represents the words which were not included in the initial contents object.

Now we need to enter numerical values for each key having empty string as its value. The values should be numbers from image file names (without zero padding). So, view images of the scanned files, look for the numbers in their file names and enter those numbers as the values for relevant keys.

We get the following code:

Replace with this code the contents of the file from which initial code was taken (in our case this was the file /data/lexicon/greek_lexicon_of_nt_by_robinson/greek_and_english_lexicon_of_nt_by_robinson_contents.js) and save it.

After doing this lexicon resource should work in sync with parsed text resource.

Workflows for multiple collections

Usually scanned resource of the type "Lexicon" is being included into several collections. E.g. such resource as lexicon by E. Robertson will be used in every collection dedicated to certain book of the New Testament. This means that the same contents file of the scanned resource of the type "Lexicon" will be used by all relevant collections.

There are several workflows for creating contents file to be used by several collections.

Supplementing in stages

One possible workflow is as follows: at first we create new contents file to be used by certain single collection and fill the gaps with page numbers for all lemmas found in the parsed text of that collection. Then we supplement the contents file with the lemmas found in parsed text of another collection and fill the gaps with page numbers of these lemmas. And we repeat this process again and again until all lemmas of the all parsed texts of the all relevant collections are included in the contents file and all relevant page numbers are filled in.

This workflow has the advantage that we can work only with lemmas of the parsed text of the single collection and doing so quickly prepare one or more resources of the type "Lexicon" to be used inside single collection. The disadvantage is that in each cycle we need again to browse through all pages of the scanned book in search for relevant lemmas and that takes a lot of time.

Supplementing at start

Another possible workflow is as follows: at first we create new contents file to be used by certain single collection. Then we don't fill the gaps with page numbers, but instead supplement the contents file with the lemmas found in original text of another collection. And we repeat this process again and again until all lemmas of the all original texts of the all relevant collections are included in the contents file. Then we browse through all pages of the scanned book, find the page numbers of the all lemmas and fill the gaps in contents file with these page numbers.

This workflow has the advantage that we must browse though all pages of the scanned book only once and this takes much less time than repeated browsing of the workflow described above. But the disadvantage is that we cannot work with the single collection at the time and must create huge contents file at once.

Cleaning page numbers

By using the first or the second workflow of those described above we get contents file of the resource of the type "Lexicon" which is being used by multiple collections. We may need to add another resource of the type "Lexicon" to the same collections. E.g. after having added lexicon by E. Robinson to every collection dedicated to certain book of the New Testament we may need to add F. Zorell's Lexicon Graecum Novi Testamenti to the same collections. In such cases we can shortcut the process by using the third workflow.

The contents file for the new resource of the type "Lexicon" should contain the same lemmas. This means that we can reuse existing contents file: we only need to remove page numbers, to change the name of the contents object and to change the name of the file. To remove page numbers from the contents file use Lexicon page numbers cleaner. Copy contents object from the contents file, paste it in the field "Lexicon contents object" and click the button "Clean page numbers":

Then save the outputted contents object without page numbers using relevant variable name and file name.

Importing after cleaning

It may happen that one resource of the type "Lexicon" has been added to multiple collections and another resource of the type "Lexicon" has been added to just single or several collections. E.g. such resource as E. Robinson's Greek and English lexicon of the New Testament has been added to every collection dedicated to certain book of the New Testament, but such resource as F. Zorell's Lexicon Graecum Novi Testamenti has been added to one or couple of collections. Now we need to add this resource to remaining collections.

In this case we need to use the following workflow. At first we should take that bigger contents file which contains comprehensive list of lemmas found in multiple collections and remove the page numbers from it. After that we need to import data into cleaned contents object from the contents object which contains less comprehensive list of lemmas from single collection or couple of collections. To do this go to Lexicon contents importer form and fill the fields:

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Language" should be "Greek" because lemmas in both contents objects are in Greek.

The value of the field "Lexicon contents object" should be contents object in which page numbers have been removed, i.e. that contents object which contains comprehensive list of lemmas found in multiple collections.

The value of the field "Lexicon contents object to be imported" should be contents object with all page numbers intact which contains less comprehensive list of lemmas from single collection or couple of collections.

After filling fields with such values click the button "Load contents" which is below the first textarea and the list of lemmas contained in the initial contents object will be displayed below the heading "Initial contents object:". Then click the button "Load contents" which is below the second textarea and the list of lemmas contained in contents object to be imported will be displayed below the heading "Contents object to be imported:". After that click the button "Import contents" and the resulting contents object will be outputted inside textarea "Resulting contents object code". Then click the button "Check for completeness". All lemmas below the headings "Contents object to be imported:" and "Initial contents object:" should be colored green. If certain lemmas remain not colored, inform about it senior editor.

Then save the resulting contents object using relevant variable name and file name.

Lexicon (transcribed)

Usually lexicon contains many hundreds of pages of text which uses complex formatting. In such situation there are no sense to create transcribed resource; scanned resource will be adequate solution.

But there are some smaller and simpler lexicons which do not use complex formatting. In such case creating transcribed resource might be considered. As an example of transcribed lexicon resource Greek-English lexicon to the New Testament by Th. S. Green has been listed in the Epistle to Titus collection.

Creating transcribed resource of the type "lexicon" involves creating one data file.

Creating data file

The text of lexicon articles should be HTML formatted according simple convention. Here is example of HTML formatted lexicon articles:

The following conventions are used to format lexicon articles.

(1) On the top of the series of articles on words starting from certain letter is that letter wrapped by "h3" tag.

(2) Series of articles on words starting from certain letter is wrapped by "dl" tag.

(3) The words which the lexicon explains are wrapped by "dt" tag.

(4) The lemmas of explained words are wrapped by "span" tags having "class" attribute value "lexicon-heading". These "span" tags have "data-lemma" attribute. The value of this attribute is lowercase lemma of the explained word.

(5) Explanation of the word is wrapped by "dd" tag. Certain word may have several explanations, so below "dt" tag may stand several "dd" tags.

(6) Inner links, i.e. the links that lead from one place in the lexicon to another place in the same lexicon are wrapped by "a" tags. Inner link anchor has "class" attribute value "pc-anchor" and "id" attribute value consisting from lowercase lemma prefixed by certain string indicating lexicon title. Inner link himself has "class" attribute value "inner-link" and "data-anchor" attribute value consisting from lowercase lemma prefixed by certain string indicating lexicon title. In code example above there is link <a class="inner-link" data-anchor="green-nt-lex-Œ≤Œ±œÅŒøœÇ" >Œ≤Œ¨œÅŒøœÇ</a> which leads to its anchor <a class="pc-anchor" id="green-nt-lex-Œ≤Œ±œÅŒøœÇ" >ŒíŒ¨œÅŒøœÇ</a>.

Using these conventions lexicon articles should be formatted. There are no definite conventions how to format introduction, table of contents, various indexes, etc. Ask about it senior editor.

If we have lexicon articles in which the words explained are wrapped by "dt" tag and explanations are wrapped by "dd" tag, for further formatting Lexicon code formatter can be used. This tool wraps the words explained by "span" tags having "class" attribute value "lexicon-heading" and "data-lemma" attribute having as value the lemma of the word:

The value of the field "Lexicon code" should be the HTML code containing lexicon articles in which the words explained are wrapped by "dt" tag and explanations are wrapped by "dd" tag

Having pasted such code in the field "Lexicon code" click the button "Load code", and lexicon articles should be rendered below the heading "Lexicon:". Then click the button "Format code" and formatted code will be outputted in "Lexicon code output" textarea. The outputted code will be as this:

HTML formatted lexicon text should be converted to javascript string. It is easy to do by wrapping HTML code by backtick (``) symbols. If there are apostrophs in the text, they should be escaped using "\" symbol. The string we get be applying backticks should be made the value of the variable whose name is the same as the shortname of the resource [LINK TO BE ADDED].

This way we get the following code:

<dd>a bag, purse, Lu. 10.4; 12.33; 22.35, 36.</dd>

<!-- part of code has been cut out -->

<dt><a class="pc-anchor" id="green-nt-lex-βαρος"><span class="lexicon-heading" data-lemma="βŒ¨ρος">ΒŒ¨ρος</span></a>, εος, τœå,</dt>
<dd>weight, heaviness; a burden, any thing grievous and hard to be borne, Mat. 20.12. Ac. 15.28. Re. 2.24; burden, charge, <i>or,</i> weight, influence, dignity, honour, 1 Thes. 2.6; <i>with another noun in government,</i> fullness, abundance, excellence, 2 Co. 4.17.</dd>

<!-- part of code has been cut out -->

</dl>

<!-- part of code has been cut out -->`;

The code should be saved in the file whose name is the same as resorce shortname, i.e. "greek_lexicon_to_nt_by_green.js" . Data file should be placed in following directory: /data/lexicon/greek_lexicon_to_nt_by_green/ .

After doing this transcribed lexicon resource should work in sync with parsed text resource.

Checking completeness

Created transcribed lexicon resource should be checked for completenes.

To do this go to Lexicon completeness checker page and fill the form:

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Lexicon code" should be full HTML code of the lexicon. Use browser‚Äôs HTML inspector (available on right-click in every major browser) to copy lexicon‚Äòs HTML code from Library app‚Äôs page. To do this right-click inside HTML inspector's panel on the "div" element having "class" attribute "tab__content-inner" and in context menu select option "Copy outerHTML":

Then paste the copied string into form‚Äòs field. After that select and delete opening and closing "div" tags from the code pasted into field:

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Parsed text code" should be HTML code of the parsed text. Use browser‚Äôs HTML inspector to copy this part of code from Library app‚Äôs page. As with lexicon's code, right-click inside HTML inspector's panel on the "div" element having "class" attribute "parsed-text-split-top" and in context menu select option "Copy outerHTML"; after that select and delete all code before first "span" tag having "class" attribute "line" and closing "div" tag from the code pasted into field:

After filling fields with these values, click the button "Load lexicon" and the lexicon text will be displayed beneath "Lexicon:" heading.

Then click the button "Load text" and the text will be displayed beneath "Parsed text:" heading.

After loading lexicon and parsed text click the button "Check for completeness" and all words beneath the heading "Parsed text:" should be displayed in green background.

If some words will not be displayed in green background, this may be for two reasons: (1) the word is not included in the lexicon (proper names are often not included in smaller lexicons); (2) the lemma of the same word in parsed text and in the lexicon are slightly different.

In the case (2) the code of lexicon‚Äòs data file should be edited.

For example, in Epistle to Titus collection parsed text data file there is such line:

` <span class="word" data-form="·ºêπηγγεŒØλατο" data-part-of-speech="verb" data-parsing="aorist middle indicative 3rd person singular" data-lemma="·ºêπαγγŒ≠λλομαι">·ºêπηγγεŒØλατο</span>`

In Th. S. Green‚Äòs Greek-English lexicon resource data file the code of the relevant article is as follows:

`<dt><span class="lexicon-heading" data-lemma="·ºêπαγγŒ≠λλω">·ºòπαγγŒ≠λλω</span>, (<a class="inner-link" data-anchor="green-nt-lex-επι">·ºêπŒØ</a> &amp; <a class="inner-link" data-anchor="green-nt-lex-αγγελλω">·ºÄγγŒ≠λλω</a>)</dt>
<dd>f. ελœé,</dd>
<dd>to declare, announce; <i>mid.</i> to promise, undertake, Mar. 14.11. Ro. 4.21, et al.; to profess, 1 Ti. 2.10: <i>whence</i></dd>`

The value of "data-lemma" attribute in parsed text code is "·ºêœÄŒ±Œ≥Œ≥Œ≠ŒªŒªŒøŒºŒ±Œπ"; the value of "data-lemma" attribute in lexicon is "·ºêœÄŒ±Œ≥Œ≥Œ≠ŒªŒªœâ". Since the values of "data-lemma" attribute in parsed text code and in lexicon code do not match, clicking on the word in parsed text pane will result into error message being displayed inside lexicon‚Äòs content panel. To avoid this we need to add another "span" tag having class attribute value "lexicon-heading" and "data-lemma" attribute value "·ºêœÄŒ±Œ≥Œ≥Œ≠ŒªŒªŒøŒºŒ±Œπ":

`<dt><span class="lexicon-heading" data-lemma="·ºêπαγγŒ≠λλω"><span class="lexicon-heading" data-lemma="·ºêπαγγŒ≠λλομαι">·ºòπαγγŒ≠λλω</span></span>, (<a class="inner-link" data-anchor="green-nt-lex-επι">·ºêπŒØ</a> &amp; <a class="inner-link" data-anchor="green-nt-lex-αγγελλω">·ºÄγγŒ≠λλω</a>)</dt>
<dd>f. ελœé,</dd>
<dd>to declare, announce; <i>mid.</i> to promise, undertake, Mar. 14.11. Ro. 4.21, et al.; to profess, 1 Ti. 2.10: <i>whence</i></dd>`

This should solve the issue. Similarly proceed with the other words which for the same reason were not displayed in the green background.

Coding policy

Dealing with alternative characters

In unicode two or more code points may encode characters which look identically or have only stylistic difference. In order for all functionality to work correctly the uniformity of encoding must be enforced by using only characters from certain "standard" set. To achieve this go to Unicode Characters changer and use the form to change unicode characters into "standard" ones.

Translation (scanned)

Creating image files

To create scanned resource of the type "Translation" you first need a series of JPG images, each image picturing one page of the book. Scanned resource always includes all pages of the book, i.e. each page from the title page to the last, not including covers and promotional materials. About creating a series of JPG files for scanned resource, read in Common tasks [LINK TO BE ADDED].

When you have a series of JPG files each image picturing one page of the book and named starting from page0001.jpg, submit them to the senior editor who will upload those files to the server. The files will be uploaded to the directory which was entered as value of the key "scanned_source_shortname" when original text resource was listed as part of collection. For example, in the Epistle to Titus collection the translation by R. Young has been listed [LINK TO BE ADDED] and the value of the key "scanned_source_shortname" is "nt_titus_tr_EN_young_contents". It means that the pictures of the pages must be uploaded to the directory /_scans/nt_titus_tr_EN_young_contents/ .

Having uploaded the images of the pages to the server, senior editor should list the scanned book as described in section Listing scanned books.

After uploading the files of the scanned book and listing it among scanned books, it can be browsed using the value of the key "scanned_source_shortname" in the URL: parsedclassics.com/reader/embedded_bookreader.html?nt_titus_tr_EN_young_contents .

Creating contents file

In order for translation to work in sync with parsed text, the contents file must be created. To create contents file go to Scanned book contents generator page and fill the form:

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Line range" should be pipe delimited line ranges. In Epistle to Titus there are three chapters, the first having 16 verses, the second ‚Äì 15 verses and the third ‚Äì 15 verses. So, the value of this field should be 1-16|1-15|1-15 .

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Prefix" should be be pipe delimited line prefixes, one for each chapter. The chapters of the New Testament are usually indicated by the number written to the left from verse number; colon usually used to separate chapter number from verse number. So, the value for this field is 1:|2:|3: .

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Contents shortname" should be the same as the value of the key "contents_shortname" which was entered while listing resource as part of collection [LINK TO BE ADDED]. The value we entered for this key was "nt_titus_tr_EN_young_contents", so we now should enter it as the value of the field "Contents shortname".

After filling fields with these values, click the button "Generate contents" and the contents code will be displayed in "Contents code output" textarea.

The code will be as this:

nt_titus_tr_EN_young_contents = {

  "title": ""

  , "1:1": ""
  
  , "1:2": ""
  
  // part of code has been cut out
  
  , "1:15": ""
  
  , "1:16": ""
  
  , "2:1": ""
  
  , "2:2": ""
  
  // part of code has been cut out
  
  , "2:14": ""
  
  , "2:15": ""
  
  , "3:1": ""
  
  , "3:2": ""
  
  // part of code has been cut out
  
  , "3:14": ""
  
  , "3:15": ""

}

Now we need to enter values for each key of this JSON object. The keys are indexes of lines of the parsed text. "title" is the index of the title of the parsed text. The values should be numbers from image file names (without zero padding). View images of the scanned files, look for the numbers in their file names and enter those numbers as the values for relevant keys.

We get the following code:

nt_titus_tr_EN_young_contents = {

  "title": "753"

  , "1:1": "753"

  , "1:2": "753"

  // part of code has been cut out

  , "1:15": "753"

  , "1:16": "753"

  , "2:1": "753"

  , "2:2": "753"

  // part of code has been cut out

  , "2:14": "753"

  , "2:15": "753"

  , "3:1": "753"

  , "3:2": "753"

  // part of code has been cut out

  , "3:14": "753"

  , "3:15": "753"

};

This code should be saved in the file having the same name as the value in "Contents shortname" field in the form, so it will be nt_titus_tr_EN_young_contents.js . The file should be placed in directory whose name is the same as resource shortname. Resource shortname is "nt_titus_tr_EN_young" so the directory will be /data/translation/nt_titus_tr_EN_young/ .

After doing this translation resource should work in sync with parsed text resource.

Translation (transcribed)

Translation (transcribed)

Creating transcribed resource of the type "Translation" involves creating one data file.

Creating data file

Data file uses certain formatting conventions.

HTML "span" tag having class attribute "verse" should wrap each line of the text.

"span" tag having class attribute "verse-number" should wrap verse number in each line. The same "span" element should also have as its class attribute the string indicating line number, such as "v1-1", "v1-2", etc. The latter class strings should be the same as in parsed text resource.

"span" tag having class attribute "para" should mark start of each new paragraph.

HTML code formatted using these "span" tags should be converted to string and made the second argument of the function "ParsedClassicsData._loadResource". The first argument of this function should be the value of the key "resource_shortname" from collection catalogue. Transcribed translation resource shortname from Epistle to Titus catalogue is "nt_titus_tr_EN_young", so this string will be the first argument.

This way we get such data file:

ParsedClassicsData._loadResource("nt_titus_tr_EN_young",

'<span class="verse"><span class="verse-number v1-1">1:1</span> Paul, a servant of God, and an apostle of Jesus Christ, according to the faith of the choice ones of God, and an acknowledging of truth that [is] according to piety, </span>' + 

'<span class="verse"><span class="verse-number v1-2">1:2</span> upon hope of life age-during, which God, who doth not lie, did promise before times of ages, </span>' + 

'<span class="verse"><span class="verse-number v1-3">1:3</span> (and He manifested in proper times His word,) in preaching, which I was entrusted with, according to a charge of God our Saviour, </span>' +

'<span class="verse"><span class="verse-number v1-4">1:4</span> to Titus — true child according to a common faith: Grace, kindness, peace, from God the Father, and the Lord Jesus Christ our Saviour! </span>' +

'<span class="verse"><span class="verse-number v1-5">1:5</span> For this cause left I thee in Crete, that the things lacking thou mayest arrange, and mayest set down in every city elders, as I did appoint to thee; </span>' +

'<span class="para"></span>' +

'<span class="verse"><span class="verse-number v1-6">1:6</span> if any one is blameless, of one wife a husband, having children stedfast, not under accusation of riotous living or insubordinate — </span>' +

'<span class="verse"><span class="verse-number v1-7">1:7</span> for it behoveth the overseer to be blameless, as God’s steward, not self-pleased, nor irascible, not given to wine, not a striker, not given to filthy lucre; </span>' + 

// part of code has been cut out

'<span class="verse"><span class="verse-number v3-8">3:8</span> Stedfast [is] the word; and concerning these things I counsel thee to affirm fully, that they may be thoughtful, to be leading in good works — who have believed God; these are the good and profitable things to men, </span>' +

'<span class="verse"><span class="verse-number v3-9">3:9</span> and foolish questions, and genealogies, and contentions, and strivings about law, stand away from — for they are unprofitable and vain. </span>' +

'<span class="para"></span>' +

'<span class="verse"><span class="verse-number v3-10">3:10</span> A sectarian man, after a first and second admonition be rejecting, </span>' +

'<span class="verse"><span class="verse-number v3-11">3:11</span> having known that he hath been subverted who [is] such, and doth sin, being self-condemned. </span>' +

'<span class="para"></span>' +

'<span class="verse"><span class="verse-number v3-12">3:12</span> When I shall send Artemas unto thee, or Tychicus, be diligent to come unto me to Nicopolis, for there to winter I have determined. </span>' +

'<span class="verse"><span class="verse-number v3-13">3:13</span> Zenas the lawyer and Apollos bring diligently on their way, that nothing to them may be lacking, </span>' + 

'<span class="verse"><span class="verse-number v3-14">3:14</span> and let them learn — ours also — to be leading in good works to the necessary uses, that they may not be unfruitful. </span>' +

'<span class="verse"><span class="verse-number v3-15">3:15</span> Salute thee do all those with me; salute those loving us in faith; the grace [is] with you all! </span>' +

""

);

Data file‚Äòs name should be the same as the value of the key "resource_shortname" from collection catalogue. Transcribed translation resource shortname from Epistle to Titus catalogue is "nt_titus_tr_EN_young", so this should be data file‚Äòs name. Data file should be placed in "translations" directory: /data/resources/translations/nt_titus_tr_EN_young.js

After doing this translation resource should work in sync with parsed text resource.

Commentary (scanned)

Creating image files

To create scanned resource of the type "Commentary" you first need a series of JPG images, each image picturing one page of the book. Scanned resource always includes all pages of the book, i.e. each page from the title page to the last, not including covers and promotional materials. About creating a series of JPG files for scanned resource read in Common tasks the sections on scanning a book, on converting PDF file to images, on batch renaming of files, on cropping images, on retouching images, on optimizing size of JPG files.

When you have a series of JPG files each image picturing one page of the book and named starting from page0001.jpg, submit them to the senior editor who will upload those files to the server. The files will be uploaded to the directory specified in catalogue file as the value of the key "scanned_source_shortname". For example in the Epistle to Titus collection the commentary edited by W. R. Nicoll has been listed and the value of the key "scanned_source_shortname" is "expositors_greek_testament_ed_nicoll_vol_4". It means that the pictures of the pages must be uploaded to the directory /_scans/expositors_greek_testament_ed_nicoll_vol_4 .

Having uploaded the images of the pages to the server, senior editor should list the scanned book as described in section Listing scanned books.

After uploading the files of the scanned book and listing it among scanned books, it can be browsed using the value of the key "scanned_source_shortname" in the URL: parsedclassics.com/reader/embedded_bookreader.html?expositors_greek_testament_ed_nicoll_vol_4

Creating contents file

In order for commentary edition to work in sync with parsed text, the contents file must be created. To create contents file go to Scanned book contents generator page and fill the form:

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Line range" should be pipe delimited line ranges. In Epistle to Titus there are three chapters, the first having 16 verses, the second ‚Äì 15 verses and the third ‚Äì 15 verses. So, the value of this field should be 1-16|1-15|1-15.

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Line class prefix" should be be pipe delimited class prefixes, one for each chapter. The chapters of the New Testament are usually indicated by the number written to the left from verse number; colon usually used to separate chapter number from verse number. Class prefix should start with the letter "v" and follow with line number prefix in which special symbols are replaced with dashes. So, we replace colons in line number prefixes, add leading letter "v" and get the value for this field v1-|v2-|v3- .

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Contents shortname" should be the same as the value of the key "contents_shortname" in collection‚Äòs catalogue. While creating collection‚Äòs catalogue for Epistle to Titus collection we entered for this key the value "lines_nt_titus_commentary_by_nicoll_contents", so we now should enter it as the value of the field "Contents shortname".

After filling fields with these values, click the button "Generate contents" and the contents code will be displayed in "Contents code output" textarea.

The code will be as this:

var lines_nt_titus_commentary_by_nicoll_contents = {

"v-title": ""

, "v1-1": ""

, "v1-2": ""

// part of code has been cut out

, "v1-15": ""

, "v1-16": ""

, "v2-1": ""

, "v2-2": ""

// part of code has been cut out

, "v2-14": ""

, "v2-15": ""

, "v3-1": ""

, "v3-2": ""

// part of code has been cut out

, "v3-14": ""

, "v3-15": ""

};

Now we need to enter values for each key of this JSON object. The keys are class names of lines of the parsed text. "v-title" is the class name of the title of the parsed text. The values should be numbers from image file names (without zero padding). View images of the scanned files, look for the numbers in their file names and enter those numbers as the values for relevant keys.

We get the following code:

var lines_nt_titus_commentary_by_nicoll_contents = {

"v-title": "189"

, "v1-1": "189"

, "v1-2": "189"

// part of code has been cut out

, "v1-15": "194"

, "v1-16": "194"

, "v2-1": "195"

, "v2-2": "195"

// part of code has been cut out

, "v2-14": "200"

, "v2-15": "201"

, "v3-1": "201"

, "v3-2": "201"

// part of code has been cut out

, "v3-14": "206"

, "v3-15": "206"

};

This code should be saved in the file having the same name as the value in "Contents shortname" field. The file should be placed in "contents" directory: /data/contents/lines_nt_titus_commentary_by_nicoll_contents.js

After doing this commentary resource should work in sync with parsed text resource.

Commentary (transcribed)

Creating transcribed resource of the type "Commentary" involves creating one data file.

Creating data file

Data file uses certain formatting conventions.

HTML "span" tag having class attribute "verse" should wrap each line of the text.

"span" tag having class attribute "verse-number" should wrap verse number in each line. The same "span" element should also have as its class attribute the string indicating line number, such as "v1-1", "v1-2", etc. The latter class strings should be the same as in parsed text resource.

"span" tag having class attribute "para" should mark start of each new paragraph.

HTML code formatted using these "span" tags should be converted to string and made the second argument of the function "ParsedClassicsData._loadResource". The first argument of this function should be the value of the key "resource_shortname" from collection catalogue. Transcribed commentary resource shortname from Epistle to Titus catalogue is "nt_titus_commentary_by_bengel", so this string will be the first argument.

This way we get such data file:

ParsedClassicsData._loadResource("nt_titus_commentary_by_bengel",
