Grammar references (transcribed)

Creating resource of the type "grammar references" involves creating data file and image files of the grammar books. The data file contains links to image files of the scanned grammar books, so the latter should be created first.

Creating image files

To create resource of the type "grammar references" you first need to have one or more scanned grammar books. To create a scanned grammar book you need a series of JPG images, each image picturing one page of the book. Scanned book includes all pages, i.e. each page from the title page to the last, not including covers and promotional materials. About creating a series of JPG files for scanned book, read in Common tasks the sections on scanning a book, on converting PDF file to images, on batch renaming of files, on cropping images, on retouching images, on optimizing size of JPG files.

When you have a series of JPG files each image picturing one page of the book and named starting from page0001.jpg, submit them to the senior editor who will list the scanned book in the file _scanned_books.js and upload image files to the server. About the file _scanned_books.js read in the section on Listing scanned books. The image files will be uploaded to the directory named according to the key in the file _scanned_books.js . For example, in the file _scanned_books.js the key of the entry for A. T. Robertson's "Grammar of the New Testament in the light of historical research" is "grammar_of_greek_nt_in_light_of_hist_research_robertson". That means that image files of this book should be uploaded to the directory /_scans/grammar_of_greek_nt_in_light_of_hist_research_robertson .

After listing the book in the file _scanned_books.js and uploading the image files to the server, the book can be browsed using its key from the file _scanned_books.js in the URL: parsedclassics.com/reader/embedded_bookreader.html?grammar_of_greek_nt_in_light_of_hist_research_robertson

Creating data file

Data file uses certain formatting conventions.

The file should contain "Grammars" heading and "References" heading both wrapped by "h2" tags. The heading "Grammars" should contain empty "span" tag having class attribute "v-title".

Below the heading "Grammars" should be list of grammars. Earch item of the list should be wrapped by "span" tag having class attribute "text_from". Every list item should contain abbreviated name of the grammar on the left and its bibliographical data to the right, separated by n-dash. Bibliographical data should be wrapped by "a" tag, having the value "_blank" of the attribute "target" and the relative URL as the value of the attribute "href".

Below the heading "References" should be list of references to grammars for the each line of the classical text. "span" tag having class attribute "verse" should wrap all references for the single line. "span" tag having class attribute "verse-number" should wrap verse number of the line. The same "span" element should also have as its class attribute the line class as in data file of parsed text resource.

Each reference to the grammar book consists of abbreviated grammar name and page number. Abbreviated name and page number should be wrapped by "a" tag having attribute "data-grammar" and attribute "data-page". The value of the attribute "data-grammar" should be the key of the relevant grammar from the file _scanned_books.js. The value of the attribute "data-page" should be the number from the name of the image file (not the number of the page pictured!).

HTML code formatted using these tags should be converted to string and made the second argument of the function "ParsedClassicsData._loadResource". The first argument of this function should be the value of the key "resource_shortname" from collection catalogue. Grammar references resource shortname from Epistle to Philemon catalogue is "nt_philemon_grammar_refs_by_parsedclassics", so this string will be the first argument.

This way we get such data file:

ParsedClassicsData._loadResource("nt_philemon_grammar_refs_by_parsedclassics",

'<h2><span class="v-title"></span>Grammars</h2>' +

'<span class="text_from">Robertson &ndash; <a href="../reader/index.html?grammar_of_greek_nt_in_light_of_hist_research_robertson" target="blank">A Grammar of the Greek New Testament in the light of historical research. By A.T. Robertson. 4-th edition. 1924. New York: George H. Doran Company.</a></span>' +

'<h2>References</h2>' +

'<span class="verse"><span class="verse-number v1-2">1:2</span>' +
' <a data-grammar="grammar_of_greek_nt_in_light_of_hist_research_robertson" data-page="301">Robertson 215</a>' +
' </span>' +

'<span class="verse"><span class="verse-number v1-5">1:5</span>' +
' <a data-grammar="grammar_of_greek_nt_in_light_of_hist_research_robertson" data-page="710">Robertson 624</a>,' +
' <a data-grammar="grammar_of_greek_nt_in_light_of_hist_research_robertson" data-page="1286">Robertson 1200</a>' +
' </span>' +

'<span class="verse"><span class="verse-number v1-9">1:9</span>' +
' <a data-grammar="grammar_of_greek_nt_in_light_of_hist_research_robertson" data-page="287">Robertson 201</a>,' +
' <a data-grammar="grammar_of_greek_nt_in_light_of_hist_research_robertson" data-page="796">Robertson 710</a>' +
' </span>' + 

'<span class="verse"><span class="verse-number v1-10">1:10</span>' +
' <a data-grammar="grammar_of_greek_nt_in_light_of_hist_research_robertson" data-page="799">Robertson 713</a>,' +
' <a data-grammar="grammar_of_greek_nt_in_light_of_hist_research_robertson" data-page="804">Robertson 718</a>' +
' </span>' +

// part of code has been cut out

""

);

Data file‚Äòs name should be the same as the value of the key "resource_shortname" from collection catalogue. Grammar references resource shortname from Epistle to Philemon catalogue is "nt_philemon_grammar_refs_by_parsedclassics", so this should be data file‚Äòs name. Data file should be placed in "grammar_references" directory: /data/resources/grammar_references/nt_philemon_grammar_refs_by_parsedclassics.js

After doing this grammar references resource should work in sync with parsed text resource.

Diagram set (transcribed)

Creating resource of the type "diagram set" involves creating diagram images and data file.

Tools for creating diagrams

For creating diagram images you need OmniGraffle program (Mac, commercial). Only Pro version is suitable, so if you own Standard version, upgrade it to Pro.

OmniGraffle is quite complex application. If you are new to it, read its documentation before starting to create syntax diagrams.

After you are sufficiently familiar with OmniGraffle, you need to install template and stencils.

Download template and stencils.

Then click on Stencils tab and right-click on any stencil name and select "Show in Finder":

In the opened Finder window locate the folders "Stencils" and "Templates":

Unzip the file _ParsedClassicsStencils.zip to the folder "Stencils". After that you should be able to see several new stencils in the Stencils tab:

Unzip the file ParsedClassicsTemplates.zip to the folder "Templates". Then go File > Resource Browser, find the folder "ParsedClassicsTemplates", select the template "pc_diagram_template" and click button "Set as Default":

Syntax diagrams use Eczar font. Download this font (the files Eczar-Bold.ttf, Eczar-ExtraBold.ttf, Eczar-Medium.ttf, Eczar-Regular.ttf, Eczar-SemiBold.ttf) from GitHub and install on your system.

Creating syntax diagrams

Syntax diagrams are being created in OmniGraffle program by dragging objects from ParsedClassics stencils to the canvas, joining them and filling text boxes.

Notice, that in stencils some objects look identical and are put into pairs. Identical looking objects are not the same: the upper one has straight line and the one below has curved line. Accordingly, use the upper when you need to draw straight line and the one below – when you need to draw curved line.

Text boxes in the stencil objects are indicated by

(1) uppercase letter ending with dot; in this case the word should be pasted on the right from the dot;
(2) uppercase letter "W"; in this case the letter "W" should be substituted with word;
(3) lowercase letter; lowercase letter is placeholder for index and should be replaced with other lowercase letter.

The diagram created on OmniGraffle canvas should be saved both as OmniGraffle document and JPG file.

The saving of created diagram is done using "artboard". Click in the toolbar the button "Artboard Tool" and select the area in the canvas which should be visible in diagram image:

Then go File > Save As and save the diagram as OmniGraffle document. The file name should contain short title of the text, chapter and line numbers. For numbers zero padding should be used: to 2 for chapters and to 3 for line numbers. For example, syntax diagram which displays lines 1-5 of the first chapter of the Epistle to Titus should be named "nt_titus_01_001-005".

After that export the diagram as JPG image. Go File > Export and in the opened modal dialogue window select the tab "JPG" and click the button "Export".

Give for the exported image the same name as you gave for OmniGraffle document.

Diagram files (both OmniGraffle documents and JPG files) should be uploaded to directory, named after the value of the key "resource_shortname". For example, in the Epistle of Titus collection the resource of the type "Diagram set" has been defined and its key "resource_shortname" has the value "nt_titus_diagrams_by_hieronymus". It means that diagram files should be uploaded to the folder /_diagrams/nt_titus_diagrams_by_hieronymus .

Creating data file

Data file uses certain formatting conventions.

HTML "span" tag having class attribute "verse" should wrap each line of the text.

"span" tag having class attribute "verse-number" should wrap verse number in each line. The same "span" element should also have as its class attribute the string indicating line number, such as "v1-1", "v1-2", etc. The latter class strings should be the same as in parsed text resource.

After one or several "span" tag having class attribute "verse" should be "img" tag having as the value of its "src" attribute the relative URL leading to diagram image.

After "img" tag should be another "span" tag having class attribute "verse" which contains info about types of clauses represented in the diagram.

HTML code formatted using these "span" tags should be converted to string and made the second argument of the function "ParsedClassicsData._loadResource". The first argument of this function should be the value of the key "resource_shortname" from collection catalogue. Diagram set resource shortname from Epistle to Titus catalogue is "nt_titus_diagrams_by_parsedclassics", so this string will be the first argument.

This way we get such data file:

ParsedClassicsData._loadResource("nt_titus_diagrams_by_parsedclassics",

// part of code has been cut out

"<span class='verse'><span class='verse-number v1-10'>Tit. 1:10</span> Ε·º∞σ·Ω∂ν γ·Ω∞ρ πολλο·Ω∂ κα·Ω∂ ·ºÄνυπœåτακτοι, ματαιολœåγοι κα·Ω∂ φρεναπŒ¨ται, μŒ¨λιστα ο·º± ·ºêκ περιτομ·øÜς,</span>" +

"<img src='../_diagrams/nt_titus_diagrams_by_hieronymus/nt_titus_01_010-011.jpg'>" +

"<span class='verse'>" +
"a, b &ndash; existencial clauses;" +
"c, d &ndash; relative clauses;" +
"e &ndash; participial circumstancial clause." +
"</span>" +

);

Data file‚Äòs name should be the same as the value of the key "resource_shortname" from collection catalogue. Diagram set resource shortname from Epistle to Titus catalogue is "nt_titus_diagrams_by_hieronymus", so this should be data file‚Äòs name. Data file should be placed in "diagrams" directory: /data/resources/diagrams/nt_titus_diagrams_by_parsedclassics.js

After doing this diagram set resource should work in sync with parsed text resource.

Audio recording (transcribed)

Creating resource of the type "audio recording" involves creating three files: MP3 sound file, data file and contents file.

Creating MP3 sound file

The resource of the type "audio recording" syncronizes sound with text. In order this to be possible MP3 file should be encoded using Constant bit rate (CBR) mode. If you don‚Äòt know constant or variable bit rate mode was used, you should convert the file.

To convert the file the program Free Easy MP3 Joiner (Win, free) can be used. The following options should be selected.

On the main program window should be selected "export format" ‚Äì mp3 and "export type" ‚Äì convert:

Then push the button "Settings", select "Specify Settings" and push "Configure" button:

In the opened window "Configure MP3 Settings" choose "Mode" ‚Äì Stereo, "Constant bit rate" ‚Äì 192 kbps (this is MOST important), "Set flags" ‚Äì deselected:

Sound file‚Äòs name should be the same as the value of the key "resource_shortname" from collection catalogue. Audio recording resource shortname from Epistle to Titus catalogue is "nt_titus_audio_by_robinson", so this should be sound file‚Äòs name. Sound file should be placed in "_audio" directory: /_audio/nt_titus_audio_by_robinson.mp3

After doing this you should be able to listen to the recording using audio controls in resources pane.

Creating data file

To see in resource pane not only audio controls, but also the text which is in sync with the sound, we need to create data file.

In the data file we need to paste the original text and before each line to mark its start time in square brackets. The start time of each line should be marked with the precision of hundredths of the second. To see when the line starts, some software should be used, such as Seventh String Transcribe! (Win/Mac, commercial).

The code will be as this:

[00:00.00]

// part of code has been cut out

[10:43.60]

Notice, that in the code there are three places where the time is indicated without any text to the right. These are starting points in the sound file where there are no text to sync with.

IMPORTANT! The time without any text to the right indicating the end of the recording is required at the end of the file, otherwise the last line will remain highlighted after playing of the recording will end.

// part of code has been cut out

'[10:43.60]\n' +

""
);

Data file‚Äòs name should be the same as the value of the key "resource_shortname" from collection catalogue. Audio recording resource shortname from Epistle to Titus catalogue is "nt_titus_audio_by_robinson", so this should be data file‚Äòs name. Data file should be placed in "audio" directory: /data/resources/audio/nt_titus_audio_by_robinson.js

After doing this the the text from the data file should be synchronized with the sound.

Creating data file can be made easier by using Audio recording data file generator.

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Data file shortname" should be shortname of the resource.

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Recorded text" should be the lines of the text with line numbers on the left of each line. Each line should be separated from the next line by new line symbol. The easiest way to get the text formatted this way is to copy and paste the text from parsed text pane. IMPORTANT! Copy and paste the text using Chrome or Opera browser, because using Mozilla browser new line symbols may be lost.

After filling the fields with these values click the button "Load text". The text will be displayed below the heading "Recorded text:". Then click the button "Generate code" and the data file code will appear in "Data file code" textarea.

Save the code in the file as described above and enter relevant numbers inside the strings "[00:00.00]" at the beginning of the each line of text.

Creating contents file

In order for audio recording resource to work in sync with parsed text, the contents file should be created.

To create contents file go to Audio recording contents generator page and fill the form:

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Contents shortname" should be the same as the value of the key "contents_shortname" in collection‚Äòs catalogue. While creating collection‚Äòs catalogue for Epistle to Titus collection we entered for this key the value "sounds_nt_titus_audio_by_robinson_contents", so we now should enter it as the value of the field "Contents shortname".

The value of the form‚Äòs field "Recorded text code" should be HTML code of the recorded text starting from the first "div" tag having class attribute value "line" and ending with the last "div" tag having the same attribute value. Use browser‚Äôs HTML inspector (available on right-click in every major browser) to copy this part of code from Library app‚Äôs page.

After filling fields with these values, click the button "Load text" and the text will be displayed beneath "Parsed text:" heading.

After loading text click the button "Generate contents" and contents code will appear in "Contents code" textarea.

The contents code will be as this:

var sounds_nt_titus_audio_by_robinson_contents = {

"v-title": 0

, "v1-1": 8.1

, "v1-2": 23

, "v1-3": 33.8

, "v1-4": 49.5

, "v1-5": 65.8

// part of code has been cut out

, "v3-11": 580.3

, "v3-12": 590.8

, "v3-13": 606.8

, "v3-14": 616.6

, "v3-15": 630.9

};

This code should be saved in the file having the same name as the value in "Contents shortname" field. The file should be placed in "contents" directory: /data/contents/sounds_nt_titus_audio_by_robinson_contents.js

After doing this audio recording resource should work in sync with parsed text resource.

Coding policy

Dealing with unrecorded lines

It may happen that certain lines, which are included in parsed text resource are not recorded inside audio recording. E.g. inside parsed text of apostle Paul's Epistle to Romans there are lines 14:24-26 which are not recorded in Th. Karvounakis's audio recording. If we ignore this discrepancy, clicking on the lines 14:24-26 inside parsed text pane will not bring in sync the audio resource. The recomended way of dealing with this situation is as follows.

First, check how long is the silence inside the sound file at the place where unrecorded lines might be. In case there are at least 0.25 second of silence for each unrecorded line, we can leave the sound file as it is and make changes only to data file and contents file. Inside data file we should to add numbers of unrecorded lines indicating that each should play 0.25 second or a little longer:

// part of code has been cut out

'[51:53.45]14:23 ·Ωâ Œ¥·Ω≤ Œ¥ŒπŒ±Œ∫œÅŒπŒΩœåŒºŒµŒΩŒøœÇ, ·ºê·Ω∞ŒΩ œÜŒ¨Œ≥·øÉ, Œ∫Œ±œÑŒ±Œ∫Œ≠Œ∫œÅŒπœÑŒ±Œπ, ·ΩÖœÑŒπ Œø·ΩêŒ∫ ·ºêŒ∫ œÄŒØœÉœÑŒµœâœÇ¬∑ œÄ·æ∂ŒΩ Œ¥·Ω≤ ·ΩÉ Œø·ΩêŒ∫ ·ºêŒ∫ œÄŒØœÉœÑŒµœâœÇ, ·ºÅŒºŒ±œÅœÑŒØŒ± ·ºêœÉœÑŒØŒΩ.\n' + 

'[52:03.20]14:24\n' + 

'[52:03.45]14:25\n' + 

'[52:03.70]14:26\n' + 

'[52:03.95]15:1 ·ΩàœÜŒµŒØŒªŒøŒºŒµŒΩ Œ¥·Ω≤ ·º°ŒºŒµ·øñœÇ Œø·º± Œ¥œÖŒΩŒ±œÑŒø·Ω∂ œÑ·Ω∞ ·ºÄœÉŒ∏ŒµŒΩŒÆŒºŒ±œÑŒ± œÑ·ø∂ŒΩ ·ºÄŒ¥œÖŒΩŒ¨œÑœâŒΩ Œ≤Œ±œÉœÑŒ¨Œ∂ŒµŒπŒΩ, Œ∫Œ±·Ω∂ Œº·Ω¥ ·ºëŒ±œÖœÑŒø·øñœÇ ·ºÄœÅŒ≠œÉŒ∫ŒµŒπŒΩ.\n' + 

// part of code has been cut out

Then we should introduce relevant changes into contents file by using Audio recording contents generator as described above:

// part of code has been cut out

, "v14-23": 3113.45

, "v14-24": 3123.20

, "v14-25": 3123.45

, "v14-26": 3123.70

, "v15-1": 3123.95

// part of code has been cut out

If there are not at least 0.25 second of silence for each unrecorded line, then we should add it. To do this use WavePad (Win/Mac, commercial) programme. Open the sound file in WavePad, select the place the silence should be inserted and go Edit > Insert Silence... > Current:

Then type the length of silence and click "Insert Silence":

Common tasks

Scanned resources

Scanning a book

The book needed for scanned resource should be scanned in full (pages from the title page to the last, not including covers and promotional materials). Each page should be scanned into separate JPG file. Scanning resolution should be at least 400dpi, scanning mode should be "color" or "greyscale".

Quite often it is more convenient to scan two pages of the book into one JPG file. In this case you will need to split each file into two files. This can be done usinge "TileMage" program (Win, free). This program places each pair of new files created into separate directory. So you will need to flatten directory structure. This can be made using program "Suction" (Win, free).

Removing watermark from PDF file

Quite often you may find a PDF file displaying scanned book. If its quality is good enough, PDF file can be used as the source of images for scanned resource. Unfortunately, quite often each page of PDF file is watermarked with some image or text, such as "Created with Cool PDF Soft". Such watermarks should be removed before converting PDF file to series of JPG images.

To remove watermark you can use Foxit Advanced PDF Editor (Win, commercial). Open watermarked PDF file, click "Object tool" in the toolbar and then click the watermark to select it:

Then in the menubar go Edit > Delete Across Pages... and in the Dialogue select "All Pages" and click the button "Delete". The watermark will be deleted from all pages:

Save the PDF file. Now it can be converted to series of JPG images.

Converting PDF file to images

To convert PDF file to series of images use conversion software "Boxoft PDF To JPG Converter" (Win, free).

To get JPG images of good quality you should set "DPI" value at least to 400 and "Quality" value at least to 75%; "Color mode" value should be "color" even in case the pages are black and white:

Bulk download of images

Quite often you may find a scanned book published in the internet as a set of .jpg failes inside some bookreading web app, as e.g. in archive.org. In this case you should copy all .jpg files of the scanned book. To copy images one by one would be tedious, so you should use tools which allow to do bulk download of the all needed files.

At first you need to generate list of URL addresses of the image files to be downloaded. To do that go to URL list generator, fill the form and click "Generate URL list" button:

The value of the field "Start number" should be the number from the URL of the first page of the scanned book.

The value of the field "End number" should be the number from the URL of the last page of the scanned book.

The value of the field "Zero padding to length" should be the length of the numbers in the file names. E.g. if the file names of the scanned images are scanned-page00001.jpg, scanned-page00002.jpg, scanned-page00003.jpg etc., then the value of this field should be "5", because the numbers 00001, 00002, 00003 atc. contain 5 positions.

The value of the field "URL template" should be URL of the scanned image with the number changed into "{index}" variable.

After you click the button "Generate URL list" the list of URLs will be outputted into Output textarea. Now you can copy this list and use it with some software providing bulk download functionality, e.g. with the program Free Download Manager (Win, free).

Using Free Download Manager at first you should copy generated URL list, then click hamburger menu, and inside dropdown click the option "Paste URLs from Clipboard":

After that you will see the dialogue as this:

In this dialogue select the folder in which downloaded images should be saved, leave the field "Create subfolder" empty and click the button "Download". All images from the list will be dowloaded into specified directory.

Batch renaming of files

Images created by the scanner or extracted from PDF file should be renamed in order to get sequence of files page0001.jpg, page0002.jpg, page0003.jpg etc. This can easily be achived using program "ReNamer Lite" (Win; free).

In order to rename as described the batch of files we need to add three rules.

1. Add rule > Serialize. Insert where: Replace current name

2. Add rule > Padding. Add zero padding to length: 4

3. Add rule > Insert. Insert: "page"; Where: Prefix

Having added these three rules click "Rename" and all files will be renamed.

Cropping images

Often images created by the scanner or extracted from PDF file need to be cropped.

To crop single file you can use the program "Photoshop" (Win/Mac; commercial).

Open in Photoshop the file to be cropped. Click the button "Rectangular Marquee Tool" on the left. The click the button "New selection" on the top. Select on the top in the dropdown "Style" the value "Fixed size". Then on the top enter pixel values in "Width" and "Height" boxes. After doing that click the top left or top right corner of the area to be selected. The selected area will be marked by dashed line:

Then go Image > Crop:

After clicking menu item "Crop" the picture will be reduced to the selected area. Then go File > Save As and save the picture as JPG file:

To batch crop the image files you can use the program IrfanView (Win/Mac; free).

Go to File > Batch Conversion/Rename:

In the top right of the window opened select the folder containing images to be cropped and click the button "Add all". Then click the button "Browse" and select the folder in which the cropped images will be saved. The select in radio group "Work As" the value "Batch conversion" and click the button "Advanced":

In the new window select the checkbox "CROP" and enter pixel values in the fields "X-pos", "Y-pos", "With" and "Height". Then select the value in "Start corner" radio group: the value "Left top" in case you need to crop the images of the left pages or the value "Right top" in case you need to crop the images of the right pages, and click the button "OK":

After that the images will be cropped and saved in the directory you have chosen.

Rotating images at arbitrary angle

The lines of the physical book often appear inclined more or less to the left or to the right in the image. In case the image has the white background this inclination of the lines can be fixed by rotating image at certain angle.

A convenient software for rotating images at arbitrary angle is "Adobe Photoshop" (Win/Mac, commercial).

Open image to be rotated in Photoshop:

Then go Image > Image Size, deselect the option "Resample Image" and click "OK":

Now click the button "Rectangle Marquee Tool" on the left and in the dropdown "Style" on the top select the value "Normal":

Then select the part of page which needs to be rotated at certain angle:

After that right-click inside the selected area and select the option "Layer Via Copy" from the context menu:

Now select the just created layer in the right pane and push the keys "Ctrl" and "t" in the keyboard. You will see the frame and the handle:

Using the handle rotate the layer at needed angle:

Now go File > Save As and inside the dialogue click the button "Apply":

Another dialogue will be displayed. For the option "Format" select the value "JPG" and click the button "Save":

Yet another dialogue will ask do you want to replace the file. Click "OK":

In the last dialogue set the value "10" or "11" for the option "Quality", values "Progressive" and "3" for the "Format Options" and "Scans" respectively. Then click "OK" and the image will be saved:

Retouching images

Images of the scanned pages may contain various defects: inscriptions or marks left be previous owners or readers, library stamps etc. It is better to remove such defects by retouching images. This is time-consuming task, so choose for scanning the copy which has the minimal number of such defects!

A convenient software for retouching images is "Adobe Photoshop" (Win/Mac, commercial). Using this program you will need Spot Healing Brush tool.

To use this tool right-click "Spot Healing Brush tool" button on the left of the window and select "Spot Healing Brush tool" in the menu:

Optimizing size of JPG files

Very often the size of JPG file can be reduced without loss of quality. This can be achieved using such programs as ImageOptim (Mac, free) or FileOptimizer (Win, free). These programs change original files, so make backup copy before running the program.

FileOptimizer program by default creates in the same directory backup files having .bak extension. Disable this feature in the Options:

Dealing with "landscape" pages

In the books which have "portrait" pages there can be some "landscape" pages. Since the Bookreader which is used to display scanned books in Library app does not allow to rotate pages, the "landscape" pages need special treatment.

At first we need to look what are dimensions of the images of the scanned book. Let's say, dimensions are 1000px with and 1500px height. Then we need to generate the image of these dimentions having as background color the color used in Bookreader of the Library app.

After that we need to rotate our "landscape" page, resize it so that its width would be 1000px and add it on the top of just generated monochrome image. The result will be as this:

"Landscape" page viewed in Bookreader will probably be too small, but it can be zoomed in order to discern the details comfortably.

Transcribed resources

Using regex

While editing code of the file of the transcribed resource, there is often the need to remove or replace certain parts of the HTML code. For example, you may need to remove "id" or "href" attributes, to remove opening or closing part of certain tags, to reverse order of tags, to extract certain numbers and put them in another place. The most efficient way to do this is using regular expressions (regex).

Regular can be used with such code editors as Notepad++ (Win, free), ActiveState Komodo Edit (Win/Mac, free) and many others.

For using regular expressions with Notepad++ code editor go Search > Replace and inside the dialogue check "Regular expression", enter regex in the "Find" field, enter another expression in the field "Replace" or leave it blank if you need to delete and click "Replace All". Or click "Replace All in All Opened Documents" if you need to make replacements in several files. All strings which match the regular expression will be replaced:

For using regular expressions with ActiveState Komodo Edit code editor go Menu > Replace and inside the dialogue click the button "Treat the pattern as a regular expression", enter regex in the "Find" field, enter another expression in the field "Replace" or leave it blank if you need to delete and click "Replace all". All strings which match the regular expression will be deleted:

Below are examples of regular expressions:

Find field Replace field Used for Tested with
\shref="([^"]*)" empty removing "href" attributes Notepad++
\sid="([^"]*)" empty removing "id" attributes Notepad++
<\s*div.*?> empty removing opening part of "div" tags Notepad++
<\s*\/\s*div\s*.*?> empty removing closing part of "div" tags Notepad++
</span> </span>\r\n adding new line after closing "span" tags Notepad++
>[\r\n]*<span ><span removing new lines before opening "span" tags Notepad++
(<a[^<>]*class="verse_num"[^<>]*>[\s\S]*?</a>)(<span[^<>]*class="verse"[^<>]*>) \2\1 reversing order of the "a" tag having class "verse_num" with the opening part of the "span" tag having class "verse" Notepad++
(<a[^<>]*data-verse="(\d+)-\d+"[^<>]*>)(\d+)(</a>) \1\2:\3\4 extracting chapter number fom attribute "data-verse" and put it before line number inside the text of "a" tag Notepad++
([0-9]+)(\s+) 1:$1 adding chapter number (in this case "1:") before line number and empty space after line number (empty space symbol not seen in "Replace" regex) Notepad++

Comparing versions of text

While editing transcribed resource, there is often the need to compare different versions of the text. This can be done using certain online text comparision tool such as available at diffchecker.com .

Alternatively a desktop program can be used, such as WinMerge (Win, free). To compare two versions of the excerpt of the text, open the program, push the keys "Ctrl" and "N". This will open program window split into two panes:

In order to see the text as wrapped lines go View > Wrap Lines:

Then paste one version of the text into left pane, another version – into another pane, and push the button "F5". Differences of the text versions will be highlighted:
